## lattice-system

A Lean 4 + Mathlib formalization project targeting general lattice models.
This project subsumes and generalizes the earlier
[ising-model](https://github.com/phasetr/ising-model) project, progressively
covering classical spin systems, quantum spin systems, Hubbard, BCS,
CAR algebras, and eventually lattice QCD.

## Design axis: graphs, not lattices

Despite the name, the **primary combinatorial abstraction in this
library is a graph `(╬Ы, E_╬Ы)`** тАФ finite for finite-volume work and
infinite for the thermodynamic-limit / algebraic-formulation work
that is a major long-term goal тАФ not "a lattice". Concrete lattices
(the 1D chain, square / cubic grids, infinite chains, тДд^d, тАж) appear
only as specific instances such as `SimpleGraph.pathGraph`,
`SimpleGraph.cycleGraph`, products of these, or their infinite
analogues. This convention follows the standard mathematical-physics
literature on many-body systems on graphs (Lieb's theorem on
bipartite lattices, the MarshallтАУLiebтАУMattis theorem, Miyao 2021
┬з3, тАж) and aligns the project with mathlib's `SimpleGraph`
foundations.

Finite-volume work uses `╬Ы : Type*` together with `[Fintype ╬Ы]`
when needed (e.g. for traces, partition functions, finite sums of
local terms); infinite-volume work drops the `Fintype` assumption
and uses graphs over types like `тДд` or `тДд^d` instead.

The bridge from a `SimpleGraph` to the pairwise coupling
`J : ╬Ы тЖТ ╬Ы тЖТ тДВ` consumed by `heisenbergHamiltonian` (and similar
operators) lives in `LatticeSystem.Lattice.Graph` (`couplingOf`).
Existing chain coupling families (`openChainCoupling`,
`periodicChainCoupling`) are characterised as
`couplingOf (pathGraph _) _` and `couplingOf (cycleGraph _) _`
respectively.

## Scope

| Area | Stage | Typical references |
|---|---|---|
| Classical spin systems | Inherited from ising-model | Friedli-Velenik, Glimm-Jaffe |
| Quantum spin systems | Current focus | Tasaki, Nielsen-Chuang (cross-check) |
| Hubbard / BCS | Medium term | Tasaki 1998, Bru-Pedra |
| CAR-algebraic formulation | Medium-long term | Araki-Moriya, Bru-Pedra |
| Thermodynamic limit (infinite graphs) | Long term, **major project goal** | Simon, Friedli-Velenik, Bratteli-Robinson |
| Lattice QCD | Longest term | Aarts, Davies |

## Refactoring conventions and review criteria

A **single-source-of-truth document** for refactoring conventions
applied as the review checklist on every pull request:
[Refactoring conventions and review criteria](refactoring-conventions.html).
Topics: test methods (decide / bridge / small-exhaustive / shim /
`#guard_msgs`), module-split criteria, generic / dedup conventions,
deprecation window policy, naming / docstring rules, linter
exceptions, public-doc synchronisation.

The companion page [Deprecation window](deprecations.html) tracks
currently-deprecated public declarations, the `since` date,
recommended replacement, and earliest-removal window.

| P0 | Project skeleton, CI, documentation infrastructure | Done |

| P1c (Tasaki ┬з2.1) | Spin-1/2 operators `┼Ь^(╬▒)` and the commutator algebra | Done |
| P1d (Tasaki ┬з2.1) | Basis states `|╧И^тЖСтЯй, |╧И^тЖУтЯй`, raising/lowering `┼Ь^┬▒` (S = 1/2) | Done |
| P1d' (Tasaki ┬з2.1) | S = 1 matrix representations (eq. (2.1.9)) | Done |
| P1d'' (Tasaki ┬з2.1) | Problem 2.1.a for S = 1/2 (Pauli basis of `M_2(тДВ)`) | Done |
| P1d''' (Tasaki ┬з2.1) | Problem 2.1.a for `S тЙе 1` (polynomial basis of `M_{2S+1}(тДВ)` via Lagrange interpolation in `┼Ь^(3)` and `┼Ь^┬▒` ladder action) | **Done for general `S тЙе 1`** тАФ `spinS_adjoin_eq_top` (Issue #458 closed in PR #490). Algebra spanned: `Algebra.adjoin тДВ {┼Ь^{(1)}, ┼Ь^{(2)}, ┼Ь^{(3)}} = тКд`. |

| P1f''' (Tasaki ┬з2.2) | SU(2) / U(1) invariance (eqs. (2.2.12)-(2.2.13)) | Done (commutativity `totalSpinHalfRot{╬▒}_commute_of_commute`, unitarity `totalSpinHalfRot{╬▒}_conjTranspose_mul_self`, and finite-form invariance `totalSpinHalfRot{╬▒}_conj_eq_self_of_commute` all proved without axioms) |

| P1f-2c (Tasaki ┬з2.2 Problem 2.2.c) | SU(2)-averaged two-site state = singlet projector (eq. (2.2.15)); integration over Euler angles `╧Ж тИИ [0,2╧А]`, `╬╕ тИИ [0,╧А]` | Done |
| P1i (Tasaki ┬з2.4) | Heisenberg Hamiltonian on the fully-polarised state: `H |sтАжsтЯй = (тИС_{x,y} J(x,y)┬╖(if x=y then 3/4 else 1/4)) ┬╖ |sтАжsтЯй` (eq. (2.4.5), `S = 1/2`); plus the ladder step `┼Ь_tot^┬▒ ┬╖ |sтАжsтЯй` preserves the same H-eigenvalue (eqs. (2.4.7)/(2.4.9), `S = 1/2`) and its iterated form `(┼Ь_tot^┬▒)^k ┬╖ |sтАжsтЯй` for every `k : тДХ`; plus `[H, ├Ы^(╬▒)_╬╕] = 0` for the global rotation (eq. (2.4.7) operator-level), the single-axis rotated constant-spin state `├Ы^(╬▒)_╬╕ ┬╖ |sтАжsтЯй` shares the H-eigenvalue, and the two-axis spin-coherent state `├Ы^(3)_╧Х ├Ы^(2)_╬╕ ┬╖ |sтАжsтЯй = |╬Ю_╬╕,╧ХтЯй` (eq. (2.4.6) for `s = 0`); plus the magnetic-quantum-number labelling `┼Ьtot^(3) ┬╖ (┼Ьtot^-)^k ┬╖ |тЖС..тЖСтЯй = (Smax - k) ┬╖ (┼Ьtot^-)^k ┬╖ |тЖС..тЖСтЯй` (eq. (2.4.9), unnormalised, lowering from highest weight) and its dual `┼Ьtot^(3) ┬╖ (┼Ьtot^+)^k ┬╖ |тЖУ..тЖУтЯй = (-Smax + k) ┬╖ (┼Ьtot^+)^k ┬╖ |тЖУ..тЖУтЯй` (eq. (2.4.9), unnormalised, raising from lowest weight); plus the Casimir invariance `┼Ьtot┬▓ ┬╖ (┼Ьtot^тИУ)^k ┬╖ |s..sтЯй = Smax(Smax+1) ┬╖ (┼Ьtot^тИУ)^k ┬╖ |s..sтЯй` for any constant `s`. For the matched highest/lowest-weight ladders, the unnormalised iterates `(┼Ьtot^-)^k ┬╖ |тЖС..тЖСтЯй` and `(┼Ьtot^+)^k ┬╖ |тЖУ..тЖУтЯй` carry `(H, ┼Ьtot┬▓, ┼Ьtot^(3))` simultaneous eigenvalues `(c_J, Smax(Smax+1), SmaxтИУk)`; plus the boundary annihilations `┼Ьtot^- ┬╖ |тЖУ..тЖУтЯй = 0` and `┼Ьtot^+ ┬╖ |тЖС..тЖСтЯй = 0` ensuring the ladder terminates after spanning all `2Smax + 1 = |╬Ы| + 1` magnetisation sectors тАФ building toward the full |╬ж_MтЯй / |╬Ю_╬╕,╧ХтЯй ferromagnetic ground-state space | Done |
| P1g | Gibbs state `╧Б = e^{-╬▓H}/Z`, `Tr(╧Б) = 1`, `тЯи1тЯй = 1`, `Z(0) = dim`, `Z(0) тЙа 0`, linearity `тЯиOтВБ+OтВВтЯй = тЯиOтВБтЯй+тЯиOтВВтЯй`, `тЯиc┬╖OтЯй = c┬╖тЯиOтЯй`, `тЯи-OтЯй = -тЯиOтЯй`, `тЯиAтИТBтЯй = тЯиAтЯйтИТтЯиBтЯй`, `тЯи╬г fтЯй = ╬г тЯиfтЯй`, `[╧Б, H] = 0`, reality of `тЯиOтЯй` for Hermitian `O`, conservation `тЯи[H,A]тЯй = 0`, anticommutator real / commutator imaginary, `(тЯиH┬╖OтЯй).im = 0`, ╬▓ = 0 closed form `╧Б_0 = I/dim` and `тЯиAтЯй_0 = Tr A / dim`, one-parameter group property `e^{-(╬▓тВБ+╬▓тВВ)H} = e^{-╬▓тВБH} ┬╖ e^{-╬▓тВВH}` and invertibility, exact discrete semigroup identity `e^{-(n╬▓)H} = (e^{-╬▓H})^n` (extended to `n : тДд` via `gibbsExp_inv`) | Done |
| P1h | Periodic boundary conditions, Heisenberg chain (open and periodic BC), Gibbs state instantiation for both BCs (Hermiticity, commutativity with `H`, ╬▓ = 0 closed form, expectation realness for Hermitian observables, conservation `тЯи[H, A]тЯй = 0`, energy expectation as a bond-sum decomposition, energy expectation real, `тЯиH ┬╖ OтЯй` real for Hermitian `O`, `тЯиH^nтЯй` real for any `n : тДХ`) | Done |
| P1j (Tasaki ┬з2.3) | Single-spin and multi-spin time-reversal map `╬Ш╠В := ├╗_2 ┬╖ K╠В` for `S = 1/2`: explicit formula `╬Ш╠В((a, b)с╡А) = (-b*, a*)с╡А` (Tasaki eq. (2.3.6)), action on `|╧И^тЖСтЯй` / `|╧И^тЖУтЯй`, additivity, antilinearity, single-spin **Kramers degeneracy** `╬Ш╠В┬▓ = -1╠В` (Tasaki eq. (2.3.8) at half-odd-integer spin), spin sign flip `╬Ш╠В(┼Ь^(╬▒) v) = -┼Ь^(╬▒)(╬Ш╠В v)` (Tasaki eq. (2.3.14)), and multi-spin Kramers `╬Ш╠В_tot┬▓ = (-1)^|╬Ы| ┬╖ 1╠В` for finite `╬Ы` (Tasaki ┬з2.3 lattice extension at `S = 1/2`) | Done |
| P1k (Tasaki ┬з2.5) | Antiferromagnetic N├йel state on bipartite chain `Fin (2K)` / 2D `Fin (2K) ├Ч Fin (2L)` / 3D `(Fin (2K) ├Ч Fin (2L)) ├Ч Fin (2M)`: state definitions, magnetisation = 0, тИИ `H_0`, per-bond `┼Ь_x ┬╖ ┼Ь_y ┬╖ |╬ж_N├йelтЯй = (1/2)|swapтЯй - (1/4)|╬ж_N├йelтЯй` for every adjacent and wrap-around bond (Tasaki ┬з2.5 (2.5.3)), per-bond expectation `тЯи╬ж_N├йel, ┼Ь_x ┬╖ ┼Ь_y ┬╖ ╬ж_N├йelтЯй = -(1/4)` (Tasaki ┬з2.5 (2.5.4) ingredient), per-bond `┼Ь^z ┬╖ ┼Ь^z` correlation `-(1/4)` and off-diagonal correlator vanishing, parallel-bond expectation `+1/4`, K=1 chain Heisenberg energy `J/2`, time-reversal `╬Ш╠В_tot ┬╖ |╬ж_N├йelтЯй` action across all dimensions, Marshall sign machinery (generic `marshallSignOf` + chain / 2D / 3D specialisations + `flipConfig` + Marshall ├Ч time-reversal bridge), the **generic graph-centric `neelStateOf : (V тЖТ Bool) тЖТ ((V тЖТ Fin 2) тЖТ тДВ)`** primitive (Tasaki ┬з2.5 (2.5.2) graph-centric form) of which the chain / 2D / 3D versions are 1-line corollaries via the `_eq_neelConfigOf` / `_eq_neelStateOf` bridges, the **Marshall-dressed standard basis** `marshallDressedBasis A ╧Г := marshallSignOf A ╧Г тАв basisVec ╧Г` (Tasaki ┬з2.5 (2.5.8)) with orthonormality and `H_M`-membership, the **realness of dressed Heisenberg matrix elements** for real coupling `J` (Tasaki ┬з2.5 p. 41, Property (i): each `((spinHalfDot x y) ╧Г ╧Г').im = 0`, hence `((heisenbergHamiltonian J) ╧Г ╧Г').im = 0`, hence the dressed bilinear pairing has zero imaginary part), the **Marshall sign trick** (Tasaki ┬з2.5 p. 41, Property (ii)): for real non-negative `J` supported on bipartite bonds and `╧Г тЙа ╧Г'`, the dressed off-diagonal Heisenberg pairing has non-positive real part, the **swap-connectivity** (Tasaki ┬з2.5 p. 41тАУ42, Property (iii)): for a connected graph `G` and any `╧Г x тЙа ╧Г y`, the configurations `╧Г` and `basisSwap ╧Г x y` are connected by a chain of single-edge swaps, and the **MarshallтАУLiebтАУMattis Theorem 2.2 in `H_0` (matrix level)**: assembled across PRs ╬▒-5a through ╬▒-5o, the shifted dressed Heisenberg matrix `B = c ┬╖ I тИТ M` (symmetric, non-negative, irreducible on `H_0`) admits a unique-up-to-positive-scalar strictly positive PerronтАУFrobenius eigenvector тАФ equivalent to the matrix-level Tasaki (2.5.4) ground-state expansion `╬г_╧Г c_╧Г \|╬и╠Г^╧ГтЯй` with `c_╧Г > 0` тАФ first five steps of the MarshallтАУLiebтАУMattis Theorem 2.2 formalization track (Issue #412) | In progress |
| P1l (Tasaki ┬з2.5, 2D / 3D Heisenberg) | 2D square-lattice + 2D torus + 3D cubic-lattice Heisenberg Hamiltonians via graph products `pathGraph (N+1) тЦб pathGraph (N+1)` and `cycleGraph (N+2) тЦб cycleGraph (N+2)`; Hermiticity + Gibbs state companion families (full 11-companion family per variant: `_isHermitian`, `_commute_hamiltonian`, `_GibbsExpectation_zero`, `_im_of_isHermitian`, `_commutator_hamiltonian`, `_mul_hamiltonian_im`, `_hamiltonian_sq_im`, `_hamiltonian_pow_im`, `_anticommutator_im`, `_commutator_re`, `_HamiltonianVariance_im`, `_partitionFn_im`, `_ofReal_re_eq`, `_pow_trace`) at parity with the 1D open / periodic chain | Done |
| P1m (Tasaki ┬з2.5, generic-S sector form) | **Spin-S MarshallтАУLiebтАУMattis Theorem 2.2 on the magnetization sector**: generalisation of P1k from spin-1/2 / `H_0` to general spin `S` (`N = 2S`) and arbitrary magnetization sector `M` via the subtype `magConfigS V N M`. Sector matrices: shifted dressed (`shiftedDressedSReMatrixOnMagSector`), dressed (`dressedHeisenbergSReMatrixOnMagSector`), un-dressed real-form (`heisenbergHamiltonianSReMatrixOnMagSector`), and un-dressed complex-form (`heisenbergHamiltonianSMatrixOnMagSector`). Bipartite raise/lower reachability (╬│-3 connectivity for general spin) lifted to the sector subtype. PF application: `IsIrreducible` (#846), positive Perron eigenvector existence (#847) and uniqueness (#848) on the shifted sector matrix. Marshall sign conjugation forward (#853) + inverse (#854) gives a real-form sector eigenvector existence with Marshall sign structure. Eigenvector uniqueness (#854) at fixed `╬╝` and eigenvalue uniqueness (#856, via dressed-sector symmetry + Rayleigh identity). Bundled real-form ground-state theorems: same-`╬╝` form (#855) and forced-eigenvalue form (#859). Complex-form bridge: complex sector matrix Hermiticity + real-тЖФ-complex eigenvector correspondence (#857, #858, #861). Complex-form existence (#860), Marshall-positive uniqueness (#862), and **strongest bundled COMPLEX ground-state theorem** `marshallLiebMattis_spinS_heisenbergSector_complexGroundState_full` (#865) тАФ the COMPLEX-Hilbert-space form of Tasaki ┬з2.5 Theorem 2.2 in the magnetization sector. Generic spin `S`, arbitrary bipartite-antiferromagnetic Heisenberg coupling supported on a connected bipartite graph, with the intermediate-existence hypothesis. The next step is the lift from the magnetization sector to the FULL Hilbert space тАФ comparing ground-state energies across magnetization sectors. | Done |
| P2 | Finite-volume Hubbard / BCS | In progress (single-mode CAR algebra; multi-mode JordanтАУWigner backbone: JW string + multi-mode `c_i`, `c_iтАа` definitions and Hermiticity, `c_0` reductions, full on-site CAR `c_i┬▓ = 0`, `(c_iтАа)┬▓ = 0`, `{c_i, c_iтАа} = 1`, adjoint `(c_i)с┤┤ = c_iтАа`, JW string idempotent `J┬▓ = 1`, site-occupation number operator `n_i` with Hermiticity and idempotency; **full cross-site CAR algebra `{c_i, c_j} = 0`, `{c_iтАа, c_jтАа} = 0`, `{c_i, c_jтАа} = 0`, `{c_iтАа, c_j} = 0` for every `i < j`**; **Hubbard chain (open + periodic BC), Hermiticity + full Gibbs companion family**; **U(1)├ЧU(1) spin symmetry: `[N_тЖС, H] = [N_тЖУ, H] = [S^z_tot, H] = 0` (Tasaki ┬з9.3.3)**; **full SU(2) spin symmetry: `[┼Ь^+_tot, H] = [┼Ь^-_tot, H] = 0` (Tasaki ┬з9.3.3)**; **all-up-spin state `hubbardAllUpState`: complete kinetic/interaction sector; Casimir `(┼Ь_tot)┬▓`; eigenvalue `S_max(S_max+1)`; Definition 11.1 `isSaturatedFerromagnet` (Tasaki ┬з11.1.1 / eq. (10.1.5))**; **SU(2) algebra: `[┼Ь^z, ┼Ь^-] = -┼Ь^-`, eigenvalue preservation and decrement by `┼Ь^-` (Tasaki ┬з9.3.3, ┬з11.1.1)**) |
| P3 | CAR algebras, quasi-local C*-algebras, KMS states | Not started |
| P4 | Thermodynamic limit, phase transitions | Not started |

## Formalized theorems

All items below are formally proved with **zero `sorry`**. Full
mathematical statements and proof sketches are in
[`tex/proof-guide.tex`](https://github.com/phasetr/lattice-system/blob/main/tex/proof-guide.tex).

### Single-site Pauli operators

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, ┬з2.1 eq. (2.1.8), p. 15. Cross-checked with Nielsen-Chuang
┬з2.1.3 Figure 2.2 (pp. 65-66, definitions), Ex. 2.19 (p. 70,
Hermiticity), Ex. 2.41 (p. 78, `(╧Г^╬▒)┬▓ = I` and anticommutation),
Ex. 2.40 (p. 77, commutator, whence the cyclic products).

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `pauliX/Y/Z_isHermitian` | `(╧Г^╬▒)тАа = ╧Г^╬▒` | `Quantum/Pauli.lean` |
| `pauliX/Y/Z_mul_self` | `(╧Г^╬▒)┬▓ = I` | `Quantum/Pauli.lean` |
| `pauliX_mul_pauliY` etc. | `╧Г^x ╧Г^y = i┬╖╧Г^z` (cyclic) | `Quantum/Pauli.lean` |
| `pauliX_anticomm_pauliY` etc. | `╧Г^╬▒ ╧Г^╬▓ + ╧Г^╬▓ ╧Г^╬▒ = 0` (╬▒ тЙа ╬▓) | `Quantum/Pauli.lean` |

### Spin-1/2 operators (Tasaki ┬з2.1)

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, ┬з2.1 eqs. (2.1.1), (2.1.7), (2.1.8), pp. 13-15.

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `spinHalfOp1/2/3` | `┼Ь^(╬▒) := ╧Г^(╬▒) / 2` (Tasaki (2.1.7)) | `Quantum/SpinHalf.lean` |
| `pauliX_eq_two_smul_spinHalfOp1` etc. | `╧Г^(╬▒) = 2 ┬╖ ┼Ь^(╬▒)` (Tasaki (2.1.8)) | `Quantum/SpinHalf.lean` |
| `spinHalfOp1_isHermitian` etc. | `┼Ь^(╬▒)` is Hermitian | `Quantum/SpinHalf.lean` |
| `spinHalfOp1_mul_self` etc. | `(┼Ь^(╬▒))┬▓ = (1/4) ┬╖ I` | `Quantum/SpinHalf.lean` |
| `spinHalfOp1_anticomm_spinHalfOp2` etc. | anticommutation at `╬▒ тЙа ╬▓` | `Quantum/SpinHalf.lean` |
| `spinHalfOp1_commutator_spinHalfOp2` etc. | `[┼Ь^(╬▒), ┼Ь^(╬▓)] = i ┬╖ ┼Ь^(╬│)` (Tasaki (2.1.1)) | `Quantum/SpinHalf.lean` |
| `spinHalf_total_spin_squared` | `╬г (┼Ь^(╬▒))┬▓ = (3/4) ┬╖ I`, i.e. `S(S+1)` with `S=1/2` | `Quantum/SpinHalf.lean` |

### Spin-1/2 rotation operators (Tasaki ┬з2.1 eq. (2.1.26))

|---|---|---|

| `spinHalfRot{1,2,3}_conj_spinHalfOp{2,3,1}` | `(├Ы^(╬▒)_╬╕)тАа ┼Ь^(╬▓) ├Ы^(╬▒)_╬╕ = cos ╬╕ ┬╖ ┼Ь^(╬▓) - sin ╬╕ ┬╖ ┼Ь^(╬│)` (Tasaki eq. (2.1.16), even-╬╡ cyclic triple) | `Quantum/SpinHalfRotation.lean` |

| `spinHalfRot{1,2,3}_conj_spinHalfOp{1,2,3}` | same-axis invariance `(├Ы^(╬▒)_╬╕)тАа ┼Ь^(╬▒) ├Ы^(╬▒)_╬╕ = ┼Ь^(╬▒)` (Tasaki eq. (2.1.15)) | `Quantum/SpinHalfRotation.lean` |

| `spinHalfRot3_mul_spinHalfRot2_mulVec_spinHalfUp` | `├Ы^(3)_╧Ж ├Ы^(2)_╬╕ |╧И^тЖСтЯй = e^{-i╧Ж/2} cos(╬╕/2) |╧И^тЖСтЯй + e^{i╧Ж/2} sin(╬╕/2) |╧И^тЖУтЯй` (coherent state, Problem 2.1.d) | `Quantum/SpinHalfRotation.lean` |
| `spinHalfRot3_mul_spinHalfRot2_mulVec_spinHalfDown` | `├Ы^(3)_╧Ж ├Ы^(2)_╬╕ |╧И^тЖУтЯй = -e^{-i╧Ж/2} sin(╬╕/2) |╧И^тЖСтЯй + e^{i╧Ж/2} cos(╬╕/2) |╧И^тЖУтЯй` (rotation of spin-down, Problem 2.2.c auxiliary) | `Quantum/SpinHalfRotation.lean` |
| `spinHalfRot3_half_pi_mul_spinHalfRot2_half_pi_mulVec_spinHalfUp` | specialization at ╬╕ = ╧Ж = ╧А/2 (Problem 2.1.e) | `Quantum/SpinHalfRotation.lean` |

| `spinHalfRot3_commute_spinHalfOp3_smul` | same-axis rotation commutes with `v ┬╖ ┼Ь^(3)` (cf. (2.1.20) along axis) | `Quantum/SpinHalfRotation.lean` |
| `hadamard` / `hadamard_mul_self` | the Hadamard basis-change matrix `W = (1/тИЪ2)┬╖!![1,1;1,-1]` and `W┬╖W = 1` | `Quantum/SpinHalfRotation.lean` |

| `spinHalfRot1_eq_exp` | `├Ы^(1)_╬╕ = exp(-i╬╕ ┼Ь^(1))` via Hadamard conjugation + `Matrix.exp_conj` (Problem 2.1.b, axis 1) | `Quantum/SpinHalfRotation.lean` |

### ZтВВ ├Ч ZтВВ representation (Tasaki ┬з2.1 eqs. (2.1.27)-(2.1.34))

The ZтВВ ├Ч ZтВВ structure is proved across files:
- S = 1/2 (projective, eq. (2.1.31)): `spinHalfRot*_pi_sq = -1`, anticommutation, products.
- S = 1 (genuine, eq. (2.1.27)): `spinOnePiRot*_sq = 1`, commutation.

See `Quantum/Z2Z2.lean` for the unified documentation.

### Spin-`S` operators (general S тЙе 0, parameterised by `N = 2S : тДХ`)

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body Systems*, ┬з2.1 Problem 2.1.a (p. 15) and solution S.1 (p. 493).

Generic spin-`S` operators live on `Matrix (Fin (N + 1)) (Fin (N + 1)) тДВ`, with `N = 2S : тДХ` (so `N = 1` тЗФ `S = 1/2`, `N = 2` тЗФ `S = 1`). Tracking issue #458 (Tasaki ┬з2.1 P1d''' general-S generalisation).

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `spinSOp3` | `┼Ь^(3) := diag(N/2, N/2 - 1, тАж, -N/2)` for `N : тДХ` | `Quantum/SpinS/Operators.lean` |
| `spinSOpPlus` / `spinSOpMinus` | raising/lowering operators with matrix entries `тИЪ(k┬╖(N тИТ k + 1))` (resp. `тИЪ((N тИТ k)(k + 1))`) on the immediate sub/super-diagonal | `Quantum/SpinS/Operators.lean` |
| `spinSOp1` / `spinSOp2` | `┼Ь^(1) := (┼Ь^+ + ┼Ь^-) / 2`, `┼Ь^(2) := (┼Ь^+ тИТ ┼Ь^-) / (2 i)` | `Quantum/SpinS/Operators.lean` |
| `spinSOp{Plus,Minus}_apply_top` / `_bottom` | `┼Ь^+` annihilates `\|NтЯй` (highest weight); `┼Ь^-` annihilates `\|0тЯй` (lowest weight) тАФ the ladder boundaries | `Quantum/SpinS/Operators.lean` |
| `spinSOp3_commutator_spinSOp{Plus,Minus}` | **Cartan relations** `[┼Ь^{(3)}, ┼Ь^+] = ┼Ь^+` and `[┼Ь^{(3)}, ┼Ь^-] = -┼Ь^-`: `┼Ь^┬▒` shift the magnetic quantum number by `┬▒1`. Proved entry-wise via `Matrix.diagonal_mul` / `mul_diagonal` (╬▓-2 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/Algebra.lean` |
| `spinSOp{Plus,Minus}_conjTranspose` / `spinSOp{1,2,3}_isHermitian` | adjointness `(┼Ь^+)с┤┤ = ┼Ь^-`, `(┼Ь^-)с┤┤ = ┼Ь^+`, and Hermiticity of `┼Ь^{(╬▒)}` for `╬▒ тИИ {1, 2, 3}` (╬▓-3 of Issue #458). The ladder adjointness follows from the matrix-entry symmetry; `┼Ь^{(1)}` and `┼Ь^{(2)}` use the `1/2` and `1/(2i)` self-conjugacy facts | `Quantum/SpinS/Hermitian.lean` |
| `spinSDiagProj` / `spinSOp3_sub_smul_mul_diagProj` / `_self_mul_diagProj` | the **diagonal projector** `P_k := diag(╬┤_{i,k})` and the eigenvalue-action lemma `(┼Ь^{(3)} тИТ ╬╗_j тАв 1) ┬╖ P_k = (╬╗_k тИТ ╬╗_j) ┬╖ P_k`, with the annihilation specialisation at `j = k` (╬▓-4 of Issue #458). Foundation for the Lagrange-interpolation polynomial decomposition: each `P_k` will be expressed as `тИП_{j тЙа k} (┼Ь^{(3)} тИТ ╬╗_j тАв 1) / (╬╗_k тИТ ╬╗_j)` in a follow-up PR | `Quantum/SpinS/DiagProj.lean` |
| `spinSOp3_mul_diagProj` / `diagProj_mul_spinSOp3` / `spinSOp3_commute_diagProj` | the **eigenvalue equation** `┼Ь^{(3)} ┬╖ P_k = ╬╗_k ┬╖ P_k` (where `╬╗_k = (N : тДВ)/2 тИТ k`), with the symmetric `P_k ┬╖ ┼Ь^{(3)} = ╬╗_k ┬╖ P_k` and the resulting commutativity. Both are diagonal-times-diagonal computations (╬▓-5 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/Lagrange.lean` |
| `mul_diagProj_apply` / `diagProj_mul_apply` / `spinSOp{Plus,Minus}_mul_diagProj_apply` | **Column/row selection** by the diagonal projector: `(A ┬╖ P_k)[i, j] = A[i, k]` if `j = k` else `0` (and dually for `P_k ┬╖ A`). Specialised to `┼Ь^┬▒` produces off-diagonal matrix units (╬▓-6 of Issue #458) тАФ the building blocks of the polynomial decomposition theorem | `Quantum/SpinS/LadderProj.lean` |
| `spinSOpPlus_mul_diagProj_succ_mul_spinSOpMinus` | **Ladder recursion**: `┼Ь^+ ┬╖ P_{k+1} ┬╖ ┼Ь^- = (k + 1)(N тИТ k) ┬╖ P_k`. The triple product collapses to a non-zero scalar multiple of `P_k`. Iterating from the lowest-weight projector `P_N` (itself a polynomial in `┼Ь^{(3)}`) yields every diagonal projector as a polynomial in `{1╠В, ┼Ь^{(╬▒)}}` (╬▓-7 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/LadderRecursion.lean` |
| `spinSOpPlus_mul_diagProj_first` / `spinSOpMinus_mul_diagProj_last` | **Ladder boundaries**: `┼Ь^+ ┬╖ P_0 = 0` (top of ladder) and `┼Ь^- ┬╖ P_N = 0` (bottom). The first/last columns of `┼Ь^┬▒` vanish, so multiplication by `P_{0/N}` (which selects that column) gives `0`. Terminate the recursion at the highest- and lowest-weight projectors (╬▓-8 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/LadderBoundary.lean` |
| `spinSDiagProj_isHermitian` / `sum_spinSDiagProj_eq_one` | **Hermiticity** of each `P_k`, and the **resolution of the identity** `╬г_k P_k = 1`. The latter is the cornerstone for the matrix-unit decomposition: combined with the off-diagonal matrix units (╬▓-6, ╬▓-7), gives every matrix in `M_{N+1}(тДВ)` (╬▓-9 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/DiagProjProperties.lean` |
| `spinSOpPlus_mul_diagProj_succ_eq_single` / `spinSOpMinus_mul_diagProj_eq_single` | **Off-diagonal matrix-unit decomposition**: `┼Ь^+ ┬╖ P_{i+1} = тИЪ((i+1)(NтИТi)) ┬╖ E_{i, i+1}` and `┼Ь^- ┬╖ P_i = тИЪ((NтИТi)(i+1)) ┬╖ E_{i+1, i}`, where `E_{a, b} := Matrix.single a b 1` is the (a, b) matrix unit (╬▓-10 of Issue #458). These are the simplest off-diagonal matrix units expressible via `┼Ь^┬▒` ladder action on diagonal projectors | `Quantum/SpinS/OffDiagUnit.lean` |
| `spinSOp3_sq_eq_diagonal` | `(┼Ь^{(3)})┬▓ = diag((N/2 тИТ i)┬▓)`. Step toward the **Casimir identity** `(┼Ь^{(1)})┬▓ + (┼Ь^{(2)})┬▓ + (┼Ь^{(3)})┬▓ = (N(N+2)/4) ┬╖ 1` for general spin (╬▓-11 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/Op3Square.lean` |
| `spinSOpPlus_mul_spinSOpMinus_eq_diagonal` | `┼Ь^+ ┬╖ ┼Ь^- = diag((i + 1)(N тИТ i))`. The product is diagonal because `┼Ь^+[i, l] ┬╖ ┼Ь^-[l, j]` is non-zero only when `l = i + 1 = j + 1`, forcing `i = j`. Combined with the analogous `┼Ь^- ┬╖ ┼Ь^+` and `(┼Ь^{(3)})┬▓`, this assembles the Casimir identity (╬▓-12 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/PlusMinusDiag.lean` |
| `spinSOpMinus_mul_spinSOpPlus_eq_diagonal` | `┼Ь^- ┬╖ ┼Ь^+ = diag(i ┬╖ (N тИТ i + 1))`. Symmetric to ╬▓-12 with `┼Ь^┬▒` swapped (╬▓-13 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/MinusPlusDiag.lean` |
| `spinSOp1_sq_add_spinSOp2_sq` / `spinSOp_total_squared` | **Casimir identity** for general spin-`S`: `(┼Ь^{(1)})┬▓ + (┼Ь^{(2)})┬▓ + (┼Ь^{(3)})┬▓ = (N(N+2)/4) ┬╖ 1`, equivalent to `S(S+1) ┬╖ 1` for `S = N/2`. Proves the irreducible spin-`S` representation has Casimir eigenvalue `S(S+1)` (Schur's lemma). The intermediate identity `(┼Ь^{(1)})┬▓ + (┼Ь^{(2)})┬▓ = (1/2)(┼Ь^+ ┬╖ ┼Ь^- + ┼Ь^- ┬╖ ┼Ь^+)` is proved using `module` (╬▓-14 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/Casimir.lean` |
| `spinSOp3_mulVec_basis` | spin-`S` eigenstate equation `┼Ь^{(3)} ┬╖ \|kтЯй = (N/2 тИТ k) ┬╖ \|kтЯй`, where `\|kтЯй := Pi.single k 1` is the `k`-th unit basis vector of `(Fin (N + 1) тЖТ тДВ)` (╬▓-15 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/Eigenstates.lean` |
| `spinSOpPlus_mulVec_basis` / `spinSOpMinus_mulVec_basis` | **Ladder action on basis vectors**: `┼Ь^+ ┬╖ \|kтЯй = тИЪ(k(N тИТ k + 1)) ┬╖ \|k тИТ 1тЯй` for `k тЙе 1`, and `┼Ь^- ┬╖ \|kтЯй = тИЪ((N тИТ k)(k + 1)) ┬╖ \|k + 1тЯй` for `k тЙд N тИТ 1`. The standard SU(2) ladder relations on the magnetic-quantum-number basis (╬▓-16 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/LadderStates.lean` |
| `spinSOp_total_squared_mulVec_basis` | **Casimir eigenvalue on basis**: `(┼Ь)┬▓ ┬╖ \|kтЯй = (N(N+2)/4) ┬╖ \|kтЯй`. Direct consequence of `(┼Ь)┬▓ = (N(N+2)/4) ┬╖ 1` (╬▓-14) тАФ every basis vector has the universal Casimir eigenvalue, reflecting that the spin-`S` representation is a single irreducible (Schur) (╬▓-17 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/CasimirEigenvalue.lean` |
| `spinSOp{1,2,3,Plus,Minus}_commute_total_squared` | **Casimir invariance**: each `┼Ь^{(╬▒)}` and `┼Ь^┬▒` commutes with the Casimir `(┼Ь)┬▓ = (N(N+2)/4) ┬╖ 1`. Direct consequence of the scalar nature of the Casimir (╬▓-18 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/CasimirInvariance.lean` |
| `spinSOpPlus_commutator_spinSOpMinus` | **Third Cartan relation**: `[┼Ь^+, ┼Ь^-] = 2 ┬╖ ┼Ь^{(3)}`. Combines ╬▓-12 (`┼Ь^+ ┬╖ ┼Ь^- = diag((i + 1)(N тИТ i))`) and ╬▓-13 (`┼Ь^- ┬╖ ┼Ь^+ = diag(i (N тИТ i + 1))`); the difference `(i+1)(N-i) тИТ i(N-i+1) = N тИТ 2i = 2(N/2 тИТ i)` matches `2 ┬╖ ┼Ь^{(3)}` (╬▓-19 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/Cartan3.lean` |
| `spinSOp1_commutator_spinSOp2` | **Cyclic SU(2) commutator** `[┼Ь^{(1)}, ┼Ь^{(2)}] = i ┬╖ ┼Ь^{(3)}`. Derived from the Cartan relations by algebraic manipulation through `┼Ь^{(1)} = (┼Ь^+ + ┼Ь^-)/2` and `┼Ь^{(2)} = (┼Ь^+ тИТ ┼Ь^-)/(2i)`: `(P+Q)(P-Q) тИТ (P-Q)(P+Q) = -2[P, Q] = -4 ┼Ь^{(3)}`, then scalar simplification `-1/I = I` (╬▓-20 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/CyclicCommutator.lean` |
| `spinSOp2_commutator_spinSOp3` | **Cyclic SU(2) commutator** `[┼Ь^{(2)}, ┼Ь^{(3)}] = i ┬╖ ┼Ь^{(1)}`. Derived from Cartan ╬▓-2 (`[┼Ь^{(3)}, ┼Ь^┬▒] = ┬▒┼Ь^┬▒`) via `┼Ь^{(2)} = (┼Ь^+ тИТ ┼Ь^-)/(2i)`: the commutator reduces to `(1/(2i)) (-┼Ь^+ тИТ ┼Ь^-) = (-1/(2i)) ┬╖ 2 ┼Ь^{(1)} = i ┬╖ ┼Ь^{(1)}` (╬▓-21 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/CyclicCommutator23.lean` |
| `spinSOp3_commutator_spinSOp1` | **Cyclic SU(2) commutator** `[┼Ь^{(3)}, ┼Ь^{(1)}] = i ┬╖ ┼Ь^{(2)}`. Derived from Cartan ╬▓-2 via `┼Ь^{(1)} = (┼Ь^+ + ┼Ь^-)/2`: the commutator reduces to `(1/2) (┼Ь^+ тИТ ┼Ь^-) = (1/2) ┬╖ (2i) ┬╖ ┼Ь^{(2)} = i ┬╖ ┼Ь^{(2)}`. Together with ╬▓-20 and ╬▓-21 this completes the standard SU(2) commutator algebra (Tasaki eq. (2.1.1)) for spin-`S` operators (╬▓-22 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/CyclicCommutator31.lean` |
| `spinSDiagProj_mul_self` / `spinSDiagProj_mul_of_ne` | **Idempotence and orthogonality** of the diagonal projectors `P_k = |kтЯйтЯиk|`: `P_k ┬╖ P_k = P_k` and `P_i ┬╖ P_j = 0` for `i тЙа j`. Combined with ╬▓-9 (`тИС_k P_k = 1`) this gives the spectral decomposition of the identity for `┼Ь^{(3)}` (╬▓-23 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/DiagProjOrtho.lean` |
| `aeval_diagonal` | **Polynomial evaluation at a diagonal matrix**: `aeval (Matrix.diagonal v) p = Matrix.diagonal (fun i => p.eval (v i))`. Foundational lemma for the Lagrange-interpolation step (╬▓-25+) тАФ lets us pull a polynomial in `┼Ь^{(3)}` (a diagonal matrix) through to its scalar action on each diagonal entry. Proof by `Polynomial.induction_on'` on monomials and addition (╬▓-24 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/AevalDiagonal.lean` |
| `spinSDiagProj_eq_lagrange_aeval` | **Lagrange-interpolation formula for `P_k`**: `P_k = aeval (┼Ь^{(3)}) (Lagrange.basis Finset.univ (spinSOp3Eigen N) k)`, equivalently `P_k = тИП_{j тЙа k} (┼Ь^{(3)} тИТ ╬╗_j тАв 1)/(╬╗_k тИТ ╬╗_j)` with `╬╗_j = (N : тДВ)/2 тИТ j.val`. Combines ╬▓-24 (`aeval` of diagonal) with mathlib's `Lagrange.eval_basis_self` / `eval_basis_of_ne`. Each diagonal projector is therefore a **polynomial in `┼Ь^{(3)}`**, which combined with ╬▓-9 (`тИС P_k = 1`) gives an explicit polynomial decomposition of `1╠В` (╬▓-25 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/LagrangeFormula.lean` |
| `spinSOpPlus_eq_one_add_I_smul_two` / `spinSOpMinus_eq_one_sub_I_smul_two` | **Inversion of the Cartesian definition**: `┼Ь^+ = ┼Ь^{(1)} + i ┬╖ ┼Ь^{(2)}` and `┼Ь^- = ┼Ь^{(1)} тИТ i ┬╖ ┼Ь^{(2)}`. The defining identities `┼Ь^{(1)} = (1/2)(┼Ь^+ + ┼Ь^-)`, `┼Ь^{(2)} = (1/(2i))(┼Ь^+ тИТ ┼Ь^-)` invert to express the ladder operators as **linear combinations** of the Hermitian Cartesian spin operators (╬▓-26 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/PMAsOneTwo.lean` |
| `spinSDiagProj_mem_adjoin_spinSOp3` / `spinSDiagProj_mem_adjoin` | **Diagonal projectors live in the algebra generated by the spin operators**: `P_k тИИ Algebra.adjoin тДВ {┼Ь^{(3)}}` (and a fortiori `P_k тИИ Algebra.adjoin тДВ {┼Ь^{(1)}, ┼Ь^{(2)}, ┼Ь^{(3)}}`). Promotes the Lagrange-interpolation formula (╬▓-25) from "polynomial-evaluation" form to "subalgebra-membership" form via `Algebra.adjoin_singleton_eq_range_aeval` (╬▓-27 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/ProjMemAdjoin.lean` |
| `spinSOpPlus_mem_adjoin` / `spinSOpMinus_mem_adjoin` | **Ladder operators live in `Algebra.adjoin тДВ {┼Ь^{(╬▒)}}`**: `┼Ь^+, ┼Ь^- тИИ Algebra.adjoin тДВ {┼Ь^{(1)}, ┼Ь^{(2)}, ┼Ь^{(3)}}`. Direct consequence of ╬▓-26 (`┼Ь^┬▒ = ┼Ь^{(1)} ┬▒ i ┬╖ ┼Ь^{(2)}`) and the fact that subalgebras are closed under `тДВ`-linear combinations (╬▓-28 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/PMMemAdjoin.lean` |
| `single_succ_mem_adjoin` / `single_succ_swap_mem_adjoin` | **Immediate-neighbor matrix units live in `Algebra.adjoin тДВ {┼Ь^{(╬▒)}}`**: `E_{i, i+1}, E_{i+1, i} тИИ Algebra.adjoin тДВ {┼Ь^{(1)}, ┼Ь^{(2)}, ┼Ь^{(3)}}`. Combines ╬▓-10 (`┼Ь^+ ┬╖ P_{i+1} = тИЪ((i+1)(N-i)) ┬╖ E_{i, i+1}`) with ╬▓-27 (`P_k тИИ adjoin`) and ╬▓-28 (`┼Ь^┬▒ тИИ adjoin`); the ladder coefficient is non-zero on the valid range and the subalgebra is closed under multiplication and scalar `smul`. Step toward expressing every matrix unit as a polynomial in `{┼Ь^{(╬▒)}}` (╬▓-29 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/NeighborUnitAdjoin.lean` |
| `single_offset_succ_mem_adjoin` / `single_offset_succ_swap_mem_adjoin` | **Arbitrary stride-(k+1) matrix units live in `Algebra.adjoin тДВ {┼Ь^{(╬▒)}}`**: `E_{i, i+(k+1)}, E_{i+(k+1), i} тИИ Algebra.adjoin тДВ {┼Ь^{(╬▒)}}` for any `k`. Induction on `k`: base case is ╬▓-29; inductive step chains via `Matrix.single_mul_single_same` (`E_{i,j} ┬╖ E_{j,k} = E_{i,k}`) (╬▓-30 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/OffsetUnitAdjoin.lean` |
| `matrix_single_mem_adjoin` | **Every matrix unit `E_{i,j}` lives in `Algebra.adjoin тДВ {┼Ь^{(╬▒)}}`**. Three-case split: `i = j` reduces to ╬▓-27 via `Matrix.diagonal_single` (`E_{i,i} = P_i`); `i.val < j.val` is ╬▓-30 upper; `j.val < i.val` is ╬▓-30 lower. Last building block before the spanning theorem (╬▓-31 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/AllUnitsAdjoin.lean` |
| `matrix_mem_adjoin` / **`spinS_adjoin_eq_top`** | **ЁЯОп Tasaki ┬з2.1 Problem 2.1.a (P1d''') general-`S`**: every operator on the `(2S+1)`-dimensional spin-`S` Hilbert space `тДВ^{N+1}` is a polynomial in `{1╠В, ┼Ь^{(1)}, ┼Ь^{(2)}, ┼Ь^{(3)}}`. Equivalently, `Algebra.adjoin тДВ {┼Ь^{(1)}, ┼Ь^{(2)}, ┼Ь^{(3)}} = тКд`. Proof: every matrix unit `E_{i,j} тИИ adjoin` (╬▓-31), so by the entry-wise decomposition `M = тИС_{i,j} M_{i,j} тАв E_{i,j}` (`Matrix.matrix_eq_sum_single`) and the linearity of the subalgebra, every matrix is in the adjoin (╬▓-32 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/SpanningTheorem.lean` |
| `ManyBodyOpS` / `onSiteS` / `spinSSiteOp{1,2,3,Plus,Minus}` | **Multi-site spin-`S` operator space** indexed by configurations `╧Г : ╬Ы тЖТ Fin (N + 1)`, with the site-embedded operator `onSiteS i A` acting as `A` on site `i` and as the identity elsewhere; site-specialised `┼Ь_i^{(╬▒)}, ┼Ь_i^┬▒`. Hermiticity preservation `onSiteS_isHermitian` lifts from single-site to multi-site (Tasaki ┬з2.5 Phase B-╬▓ ╬▓-3a, Issue #412) | `Quantum/SpinS/MultiSite.lean` |

| `flipConfig` / `flipConfig_apply` / `flipConfig_involutive` | the spin-flip on a many-body configuration `╧Г : ╬Ы тЖТ Fin 2`: `flipConfig ╧Г x := 1 - ╧Г x`; involutive | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `timeReversalSign` / `timeReversalSign_zero` / `_one` / `_mul_flip` | per-site sign factor `╬╡(0) = 1`, `╬╡(1) = -1` for the multi-spin time-reversal, with `╬╡(s) ┬╖ ╬╡(1 - s) = -1` | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti` | multi-spin time-reversal map (Tasaki ┬з2.3 lattice extension, `S = 1/2`): `(╬Ш╠В_tot v) ╧Д := (тИП_x ╬╡(╧Д x)) ┬╖ conj(v (flip ╧Д))` for finite `╬Ы` | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `timeReversalSign_prod_conj` / `timeReversalSign_prod_mul_flip` | the product `тИП_x ╬╡(╧Д x)` is real (conjugation invariant); the cross product equals `(-1)^|╬Ы|` | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_sq` | **Multi-spin Kramers degeneracy at `S = 1/2`** (Tasaki ┬з2.3 half-odd-integer extension): `╬Ш╠В_tot┬▓ = (-1)^|╬Ы| ┬╖ 1╠В` тАФ `+1╠В` when `|╬Ы|` is even, `-1╠В` when odd | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_basisVec` | action of `╬Ш╠В_tot` on a many-body basis state: `╬Ш╠В_tot |╬и_╧ГтЯй = (тИП_x ╬╡(flip ╧Г x)) ┬╖ |╬и_{flip ╧Г}тЯй` тАФ natural many-body generalisation of `╬Ш╠В|тЖСтЯй = |тЖУтЯй` and `╬Ш╠В|тЖУтЯй = -|тЖСтЯй` | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_onSite_pauliZ_mulVec` | multi-site sign-flip equivariance for `╧Г^z` (Tasaki ┬з2.3 (2.3.14) lifted to many-body): `╬Ш╠В_tot ((onSite x ╧Г^z) v) = (-(onSite x ╧Г^z))(╬Ш╠В_tot v)`. Diagonal-action case; `╧Г^x`, `╧Г^y` deferred | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `siteFlipAt` / `siteFlipAt_self` / `siteFlipAt_of_ne` / `flipConfig_siteFlipAt_comm` / `siteFlipAt_involutive` | per-site flip helpers: `siteFlipAt ╧Д x` flips slot `x` only; commutes with `flipConfig`; involutive. | `onSite_pauliX_mulVec_basisVec` | basis-state action of the off-diagonal site Pauli: `(onSite x ╧Г^x).mulVec |╬и_╧ГтЯй = |╬и_{siteFlipAt ╧Г x}тЯй` (the spin at site `x` is swapped) | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `pauliX_eq_indicator` / `onSite_pauliX_mulVec_apply` | closed-form `pauliX a b = if b = 1 - a then 1 else 0`, lifted to `((onSite x ╧Г^x).mulVec v) ╧Д = v (siteFlipAt ╧Д x)` for any state `v` (general extension of the basis-state action) | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `timeReversalSign_prod_siteFlipAt` | `тИП_y ╬╡((siteFlipAt ╧Д x) y) = -(тИП_y ╬╡(╧Д y))` тАФ the per-site flip swaps `╬╡(╧Д x)` with `╬╡(1 - ╧Д x) = -╬╡(╧Д x)`, flipping the total sign | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_onSite_pauliX_mulVec` | multi-site sign-flip equivariance for `╧Г^x` (Tasaki ┬з2.3 (2.3.14) at ╬▒ = 1): `╬Ш╠В_tot ((onSite x ╧Г^x) v) = (-(onSite x ╧Г^x))(╬Ш╠В_tot v)` | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_onSite_pauliY_mulVec` | multi-site sign-flip equivariance for `╧Г^y` (Tasaki ┬з2.3 (2.3.14) at ╬▒ = 2): `╬Ш╠В_tot ((onSite x ╧Г^y) v) = (-(onSite x ╧Г^y))(╬Ш╠В_tot v)`. | `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_add` / `_smul` / `_real_smul` | multi-spin `╬Ш╠В_tot` is additive, antilinear in the scalar (`╬Ш╠В_tot(c тАв v) = conj(c) тАв ╬Ш╠В_tot v`), and real-linear (special case of antilinearity at real `r`) тАФ foundational for lifting Pauli-axis equivariance to bilinear / Heisenberg-type Hamiltonian forms | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_onSite_spinHalfOp{1,2,3}_mulVec` | Tasaki ┬з2.3 (2.3.14) for spin-1/2 ops `┼Ь^(╬▒) = ╧Г^(╬▒) / 2`: `╬Ш╠В_tot ((onSite x ┼Ь^(╬▒)) v) = (-(onSite x ┼Ь^(╬▒)))(╬Ш╠В_tot v)` for ╬▒ = 1, 2, 3 тАФ direct corollaries of the Pauli versions by scalar (1/2) multiplication | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_spinHalfDot_mulVec` | **Time-reversal invariance of the bilinear `┼Ь_x ┬╖ ┼Ь_y`** (Tasaki ┬з2.3): `╬Ш╠В_tot ((┼Ь_x ┬╖ ┼Ь_y) v) = (┼Ь_x ┬╖ ┼Ь_y)(╬Ш╠В_tot v)` тАФ two equivariance `-1` factors cancel; sums per-axis | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_heisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec` | **Time-reversal invariance of the Heisenberg Hamiltonian** (Tasaki ┬з2.3): for real coupling `J` (`conj(J(x,y)) = J(x,y)`), `╬Ш╠В_tot ((H J) v) = (H J)(╬Ш╠В_tot v)`. | `openChainCoupling_conj` / `periodicChainCoupling_conj` | every entry of `openChainCoupling N J` (resp. `periodicChainCoupling N J`) is real (under complex conjugation), since `J : тДЭ` makes `(-(J : тДВ))` real-valued | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |
| `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_openChainHeisenberg_mulVec` / `_periodicChainHeisenberg_mulVec` / `_squareLatticeHeisenberg_mulVec` / `_squareTorusHeisenberg_mulVec` / `_cubicLatticeHeisenberg_mulVec` | concrete time-reversal invariance: the open / periodic chain, the 2D open square / torus, and the 3D cubic Heisenberg Hamiltonians all commute with `╬Ш╠В_tot` for any real coupling `J : тДЭ`. | `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_basisVec_upDown` / `_basisVec_basisSwap_upDown` | `╬Ш╠В_tot |тЖСтЖУтЯй = -|тЖУтЖСтЯй` and `╬Ш╠В_tot |тЖУтЖСтЯй = -|тЖСтЖУтЯй` on `Fin 2` | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_singlet` | the two-site spin singlet `|тЖСтЖУтЯй - |тЖУтЖСтЯй` is **time-reversal invariant** (Tasaki ┬з2.3 / ┬зA.3): being the SU(2) `S = 0` representation, it survives `╬Ш╠В_tot` unchanged | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_triplet_zero` | the triplet `m = 0` state `|тЖСтЖУтЯй + |тЖУтЖСтЯй` is **anti-invariant** under `╬Ш╠В_tot`: `╬Ш╠В_tot (|тЖСтЖУтЯй + |тЖУтЖСтЯй) = -(|тЖСтЖУтЯй + |тЖУтЖСтЯй)` (the symmetric combination picks up a minus sign from the per-basis-vector flip) | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |

### Multi-body operator space (abstract lattice)

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, ┬з2.2, pp. 21-26 (tensor-product Hilbert space and site-local
operators). The lattice `╬Ы` is an arbitrary finite set with decidable
equality; specializing to `╬Ы = Fin N` recovers an `N`-site chain.

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `ManyBodyOp ╬Ы` | `Matrix (╬Ы тЖТ Fin 2) (╬Ы тЖТ Fin 2) тДВ` | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `onSite i A` | site-embedded operator at `i : ╬Ы` | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `onSite_isHermitian` | `A.IsHermitian тЖТ (onSite i A).IsHermitian` | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `onSite_add`, `onSite_sub`, `onSite_zero`, `onSite_smul`, `onSite_one` | linearity of the site embedding and `onSite i 1 = 1` | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `onSite_mul_onSite_of_ne` | distinct-site commutation (Tasaki (2.2.6), `x тЙа y`, S = 1/2) | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `basisVec` / `onSite_mulVec_basisVec` | tensor-product basis states and their action under site operators (Tasaki (2.2.1)/(2.2.4)) | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `onSite_mul_onSite_same` | same-site product `onSite i A ┬╖ onSite i B = onSite i (A ┬╖ B)` (Tasaki (2.2.6), `x = y`) | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `onSite_commutator_same` | same-site commutator `[onSite i A, onSite i B] = onSite i [A, B]` | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `Matrix.IsHermitian.mul_of_commute` | commuting Hermitians multiply Hermitian | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |

(2.2.10)); the `_zero` specialisation places it in `H_0` when `╬г_x ╧Г_x = 0` | `Quantum/MarshallDressedBasis.lean` |
| `spinHalfDot_apply_im_eq_zero` | every matrix entry of the two-site spin product `┼Ь_x ┬╖ ┼Ь_y` is **real**: `((spinHalfDot x y) ╧Г ╧Г').im = 0` for all `x, y, ╧Г, ╧Г'`. Case analysis on `x = y` / parallel / antiparallel via the existing `spinHalfDot_mulVec_basisVec_{parallel,antiparallel}` action lemmas. **Property (i) ingredient** for the MarshallтАУLiebтАУMattis theorem (Tasaki ┬з2.5, p. 41) | `Quantum/MarshallLiebMattis/Realness.lean` |

| `dot_marshallDressed_heisenbergHamiltonian_marshallDressed_im_eq_zero` | **MLM Property (i)**: for real coupling `J`, the dressed Heisenberg bilinear pairing `╬г_╧Д \|╬и╠Г^╧ГтЯй ╧Д ┬╖ (H ┬╖ \|╬и╠Г^{╧Г'}тЯй) ╧Д` is real (Tasaki ┬з2.5, p. 41 in the proof of Theorem 2.2). | `marshallSignOf_mul_marshallSignOf_basisSwap_of_bipartite_antiparallel` | **Marshall sign relation**: for a bond `{x, y}` crossing the bipartition (`A x тЙа A y`) with `╧Г` antiparallel at `{x, y}` (`╧Г x тЙа ╧Г y`), `marshallSignOf A ╧Г * marshallSignOf A (basisSwap ╧Г x y) = -1`. The combined product over `╬Ы` of pairwise factors collapses: outside `{x, y}` each pairwise factor is `(┬▒1)┬▓ = 1`; at the unique site in `A тИй {x, y}` the pair contributes `(-1)^(╧Г x + ╧Г y) = -1` since `╧Г x тЙа ╧Г y`; the other site of `{x, y}` lies outside `A` and contributes `1` | `Quantum/MarshallLiebMattis/MarshallSignTrick.lean` |

| `bipartiteToyMinEnergyPredictedSymm_re_neg_of_nondegenerate` | **strict negativity of the predicted symmetric min energy** (non-degenerate case): `(bipartiteToyMinEnergyPredictedSymm A N).re < 0` when both `\|A\| тЙе 1`, `\|┬мA\| тЙе 1`, and `N тЙе 1`. | `basisVec_mem_magnetizationSubspace` | `|╧ГтЯй тИИ H_{|╧Г|/2}` тАФ basis states lie in their magnetization subspace | `Quantum/MagnetizationSubspace.lean` |
| `magnetizationSubspace_disjoint` | distinct sectors `H_M тКУ H_{M'} = тКе` (`M тЙа M'`) тАФ eigenvalue uniqueness | `Quantum/MagnetizationSubspace.lean` |
| `iSup_magnetizationSubspace_eq_top` | `тиЖ_M H_M = тКд` тАФ every vector decomposes as a sum across sectors | `Quantum/MagnetizationSubspace.lean` |
| `magnetizationSubspace_eq_eigenspace` | bridge `H_M = (┼Ь_tot^(3) as End).eigenspace M` (used to inherit `iSupIndep`) | `Quantum/MagnetizationSubspace.lean` |
| `magnetizationSubspace_iSupIndep` | `iSupIndep`: each sector is disjoint from the supremum of all others | `Quantum/MagnetizationSubspace.lean` |
| `magnetizationSubspace_isInternal` | `DirectSum.IsInternal`: full direct-sum decomposition `H = тКХ_M H_M` (Tasaki eqs. (2.2.9)/(2.2.10)) | `Quantum/MagnetizationSubspace.lean` |

### Two-site spin inner product (Tasaki ┬з2.2 eq. (2.2.16))

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, ┬з2.2 eq. (2.2.16), p. 24.

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `spinHalfDot x y` | `┼Ь_x ┬╖ ┼Ь_y := ╬г_{╬▒} onSite x ┼Ь^(╬▒) ┬╖ onSite y ┼Ь^(╬▒)` | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `spinHalfDot_eq_plus_minus` | `┼Ь_x ┬╖ ┼Ь_y = (1/2)(┼Ь_x^+ ┼Ь_y^- + ┼Ь_x^- ┼Ь_y^+) + ┼Ь_x^(3) ┼Ь_y^(3)` (Tasaki (2.2.16)) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `spinHalfDot_comm` | `┼Ь_x ┬╖ ┼Ь_y = ┼Ь_y ┬╖ ┼Ь_x` | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `spinHalfDot_self` | `┼Ь_x ┬╖ ┼Ь_x = (3/4) ┬╖ 1` (the S(S+1) = 3/4 identity for S = 1/2) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `spinHalfDot_isHermitian` | `┼Ь_x ┬╖ ┼Ь_y` is Hermitian | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `totalSpinHalfSquared_eq_sum_dot` | `(┼Ь_tot)┬▓ = ╬г_{x,y} ┼Ь_x ┬╖ ┼Ь_y` | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `spinHalfPairSpinSq` / `spinHalfPairSpinSq_eq` | `(┼Ь_x + ┼Ь_y)┬▓ = 2┬╖(┼Ь_x ┬╖ ┼Ь_y) + ┼Ь_x ┬╖ ┼Ь_x + ┼Ь_y ┬╖ ┼Ь_y` (Tasaki (2.2.18)) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `spinHalfDot_commutator_totalSpinHalfOp{1,2,3}` | `[┼Ь_x ┬╖ ┼Ь_y, ┼Ь_tot^(╬▒)] = 0` for ╬▒ тИИ {1, 2, 3} (SU(2) invariance, Tasaki (2.2.17)) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `spinHalfDot_commutator_totalSpinHalfOpPlus/Minus` | `[┼Ь_x ┬╖ ┼Ь_y, ┼Ь^┬▒_tot] = 0` (ladder-operator version of SU(2) invariance) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `spinHalfDot_mulVec_basisVec_parallel` | `┼Ь_x ┬╖ ┼Ь_y |╧ГтЯй = (1/4) |╧ГтЯй` when `╧Г x = ╧Г y` and `x тЙа y` (Tasaki (2.2.19) parallel case) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `spinHalfDot_mulVec_basisVec_both_up/down` | `┼Ь_x ┬╖ ┼Ь_y |тЖСтЖСтЯй = (1/4) |тЖСтЖСтЯй`, `┼Ь_x ┬╖ ┼Ь_y |тЖУтЖУтЯй = (1/4) |тЖУтЖУтЯй` (Tasaki (2.2.19) triplet `m = ┬▒1`) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `basisSwap` / `basisSwap_involutive` / `basisSwap_antiparallel` | site-swap of `╧Г` at `x, y`, involutive and preserves anti-parallelism | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `spinHalfDot_mulVec_basisVec_antiparallel` | `┼Ь_x ┬╖ ┼Ь_y |╧ГтЯй = (1/2) |swap ╧ГтЯй - (1/4) |╧ГтЯй` when `╧Г x тЙа ╧Г y` (anti-parallel case) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `spinHalfDot_mulVec_singlet` | singlet eigenvalue `┼Ь_x ┬╖ ┼Ь_y (|╧ГтЯй - |swap ╧ГтЯй) = -(3/4) (|╧ГтЯй - |swap ╧ГтЯй)` (Tasaki (2.2.19) singlet `S = 0`) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `spinHalfDot_mulVec_triplet_anti` | triplet `m = 0` eigenvalue `┼Ь_x ┬╖ ┼Ь_y (|╧ГтЯй + |swap ╧ГтЯй) = (1/4) (|╧ГтЯй + |swap ╧ГтЯй)` (Tasaki (2.2.19) triplet `m = 0`) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian` | `H = ╬г_{x,y} J(x,y) ┼Ь_x ┬╖ ┼Ь_y` (general Heisenberg-type Hamiltonian) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_commutator_totalSpinHalfOp{1,2,3}` | `[H, ┼Ь_tot^(╬▒)] = 0` for all axes (Tasaki (2.2.13) SU(2) invariance) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_commutator_totalSpinHalfOp{Plus,Minus}` | `[H, ┼Ь^┬▒_tot] = 0` (ladder form of SU(2) invariance) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_commute_totalSpinHalfSquared` | `Commute H ┼Ьtot┬▓` тАФ the Casimir operator-level form of SU(2) invariance (consequence of `[H, ┼Ьtot^╬▒] = 0` for each ╬▒, via `Commute.mul_right` and `.add_right`) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_preserves_totalSpinHalfSquared_eigenvalue` | if `┼Ьtot┬▓ ┬╖ v = S ┬╖ v` then `┼Ьtot┬▓ ┬╖ (H ┬╖ v) = S ┬╖ (H ┬╖ v)` тАФ operator-level simultaneous diagonalisation of `H` and the SU(2) Casimir | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `spinHalfOpPlus_mul_pauliZ` / `pauliZ_mul_spinHalfOpPlus` | `╧Г^+ ┬╖ ╧Г^z = -╧Г^+` and `╧Г^z ┬╖ ╧Г^+ = ╧Г^+` тАФ the (anti)commutation at the single-site Pauli algebra level, used for the Jordan-Wigner cross-site CAR | `Quantum/SpinHalfBasis.lean` |
| `totalSpinHalfSquared_mulVec_basisVec_const` | `┼Ь_tot┬▓ |s s тАж sтЯй = (N(N+2)/4) |s s тАж sтЯй` for any constant `s : Fin 2` (Casimir eigenvalue at maximum total spin `S = N/2`) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `totalSpinHalfSquared_mulVec_basisVec_all_up/down` | specializations of the above to `s = 0` (all-up) and `s = 1` (all-down) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `totalSpinHalfSquared_mulVec_totalSpinHalfOp{Minus,Plus}_pow_basisVec_const` | for any `s : Fin 2` and `k : тДХ`, `┼Ьtot┬▓ ┬╖ (┼Ьtot^тИУ)^k ┬╖ |sтАжsтЯй = (|╬Ы|┬╖(|╬Ы|+2)/4) ┬╖ (┼Ьtot^тИУ)^k ┬╖ |sтАжsтЯй` тАФ the iterated ladder iterates remain in the maximum-total-spin SU(2) representation `S = Smax = |╬Ы|/2` (Casimir invariance, Tasaki ┬з2.4) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_basisVec_const` | `H |sтАжsтЯй = (╬г_{x,y} J(x,y)┬╖(if x=y then 3/4 else 1/4)) ┬╖ |sтАжsтЯй` тАФ every Heisenberg-type Hamiltonian acts on a uniformly-aligned basis state as a scalar; bilinear-sum lift of Tasaki ┬з2.4 eq. (2.4.5), p. 32 (`-┼Ь_x┬╖┼Ь_y |╬жтЖСтЯй = -S┬▓ |╬жтЖСтЯй` for `S = 1/2`, `x тЙа y`), with the diagonal `S(S+1) = 3/4` contribution recorded explicitly | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_basisVec_all_up/down` | specialisations of the above to `s = 0` (all-up) / `s = 1` (all-down) тАФ the eigenvector property of the fully-polarised states; ground-state status (Tasaki's `E_GS = -|B|┬╖S┬▓`) requires extra ferromagnetic structure on `J` and is not asserted here | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_totalSpinHalfOpPlus_basisVec_const` | `H ┬╖ (┼Ь_tot^+ ┬╖ |sтАжsтЯй) = c_J ┬╖ (┼Ь_tot^+ ┬╖ |sтАжsтЯй)` тАФ `┼Ь_tot^+` preserves the H-eigenvalue on a constant-spin basis state (corollary of SU(2) invariance, Tasaki ┬з2.4 (2.4.7), p. 33) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_totalSpinHalfOpMinus_basisVec_const` | same with `┼Ь_tot^-` тАФ the canonical lowering ladder Tasaki uses to enumerate the ferromagnetic ground states `|╬ж_MтЯй` (eq. (2.4.9), p. 33) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_totalSpinHalfOpMinus_pow_basisVec_const` | iterated form: for any constant `s : Fin 2` and any `k : тДХ`, `H ┬╖ ((┼Ь_tot^-)^k ┬╖ |sтАжsтЯй) = c_J ┬╖ ((┼Ь_tot^-)^k ┬╖ |sтАжsтЯй)`; specialised at `s = 0` this gives the unnormalised Tasaki ┬з2.4 (2.4.9), p. 33 тАФ every iterate `(┼Ь_tot^-)^k ┬╖ |╬жтЖСтЯй` lies in the same H-eigenspace as `|╬жтЖСтЯй` | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_totalSpinHalfOpPlus_pow_basisVec_const` | companion iterated form for `┼Ь_tot^+`: for any constant `s : Fin 2` and any `k : тДХ`, `H ┬╖ ((┼Ь_tot^+)^k ┬╖ |sтАжsтЯй) = c_J ┬╖ ((┼Ь_tot^+)^k ┬╖ |sтАжsтЯй)` (corollary of SU(2) invariance, Tasaki ┬з2.4 (2.4.7), iterated) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_commute_totalSpinHalfRot{1,2,3}` | for any `J` and `╬╕ : тДЭ`, `H` commutes with the global rotation `├Ы^(╬▒)_╬╕ = exp(-i╬╕ ┼Ь_tot^╬▒)` (composes `heisenbergHamiltonian_commutator_totalSpinHalfOp{╬▒}` with `totalSpinHalfRot{╬▒}_commute_of_commute`; the operator-level form of Tasaki ┬з2.4 (2.4.7), p. 33) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_totalSpinHalfRot{1,2,3}_basisVec_const` | for any `J`, `╬╕`, and constant `s : Fin 2`, `H ┬╖ (├Ы^(╬▒)_╬╕ ┬╖ |sтАжsтЯй) = c_J ┬╖ (├Ы^(╬▒)_╬╕ ┬╖ |sтАжsтЯй)` тАФ the rotated (single-axis) constant-spin state shares the H-eigenvalue (Tasaki ┬з2.4 (2.4.7), p. 33) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_totalSpinHalfRot32_basisVec_const` | for any `J`, `╬╕`, `╧Х`, and constant `s : Fin 2`, `H ┬╖ (├Ы^(3)_╧Х ┬╖ ├Ы^(2)_╬╕ ┬╖ |sтАжsтЯй) = c_J ┬╖ (├Ы^(3)_╧Х ┬╖ ├Ы^(2)_╬╕ ┬╖ |sтАжsтЯй)` тАФ the two-step spin-coherent state of Tasaki eq. (2.4.6) (`|╬Ю_╬╕,╧ХтЯй` for `s = 0`) is an H-eigenvector with the same eigenvalue as the constant configuration (Tasaki eq. (2.4.7), p. 33) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `totalSpinHalfSquared_mulVec_two_site_singlet` | `┼Ь_tot┬▓ (|тЖСтЖУтЯй - |тЖУтЖСтЯй) = 0` for `╬Ы = Fin 2` (singlet, `S = 0`) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `totalSpinHalfSquared_mulVec_two_site_triplet_zero` | `┼Ь_tot┬▓ (|тЖСтЖУтЯй + |тЖУтЖСтЯй) = 2(|тЖСтЖУтЯй + |тЖУтЖСтЯй)` for `╬Ы = Fin 2` (triplet `m = 0`, `S = 1`) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `totalSpinHalfOp3_mulVec_two_site_singlet` | the two-site singlet has zero `┼Ь_tot^(3)` magnetization | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `onSite_commutator_totalOnSite` | `[onSite x S╬▒, ╬г_z onSite z S╬▓] = onSite x [S╬▒, S╬▓]` | `Quantum/TotalSpin.lean` |

### One-dimensional open-chain quantum Ising

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, ┬з3.3 eq. (3.3.1), p. 55 (transverse-field Ising on an open
chain). Our formalization uses the Pauli convention `╧Г = 2┬╖S` and an
explicit bond coupling `J`.

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `quantumIsingHamiltonian N J h` | `H = -J ╬г ╧Г^z_i ╧Г^z_{i+1} - h ╬г ╧Г^x_i` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `quantumIsingHamiltonian_isHermitian` | `H` is Hermitian for real `J`, `h` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `spinZDot x y` | the Ising bond operator `╧Г^z_x ┬╖ ╧Г^z_y` (generic in `╬Ы`) | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `spinZDot_isHermitian` | each bond operator is Hermitian | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `isingHamiltonianGeneric (J : ╬Ы тЖТ ╬Ы тЖТ тДВ) (h : тДВ)` | **graph-friendly** Ising Hamiltonian `╬г J(x,y) ╧Г^z_x ╧Г^z_y тИТ h ╬г ╧Г^x_x` for any finite `╬Ы` and pairwise coupling `J`; specialises to chain / graph / lattice via the choice of `J` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `isingHamiltonianGeneric_isHermitian` | Hermitian for entry-wise real `J` and real `h` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `isingHamiltonianOnGraph G J h` | graph wrapper: `isingHamiltonianGeneric (couplingOf G J) h`; double-sum convention matches Heisenberg-on-graph | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `isingHamiltonianOnGraph_isHermitian` | Hermitian for real `J, h` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `isingGibbsStateOnGraph G ╬▓ J h` | Gibbs state of the graph-built Ising Hamiltonian | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `isingGibbsStateOnGraph_isHermitian` / `isingGibbsStateOnGraph_commute_hamiltonian` | Hermiticity (real `J, h`) and commute with the Hamiltonian | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `LatticeSystem.Lattice.sum_pathGraph_forward` / `sum_pathGraph_backward` / `sum_pathGraph_adj` | sum-decomposition helpers for `pathGraph (N+1)` adjacency: `╬г_{x,y}` over ordered adjacent pairs = `╬г_{i:Fin N} (f i.cs i.s + f i.s i.cs)` | `Lattice/Graph.lean` |
| `pathGraphParityColoring` / `pathGraph_isBipartite` | parity-based 2-colouring of `pathGraph (N + 1)` (`i тЖж i.val % 2`) and the corresponding `IsBipartite` proof. Underpins the N├йel state (`Quantum/NeelState.lean`) and the Marshall-Lieb-Mattis theorem (Tasaki ┬з2.5) | `Lattice/Graph.lean` |
| `cycleGraphEvenParityColoring` / `cycleGraph_even_isBipartite` | parity-based 2-colouring of the even cycle `cycleGraph (2 * K + 2)` and the corresponding `IsBipartite` proof. Wrap-around case `(2K+1) + 1 тЙб 0` still flips parity because the cycle length is even (odd cycles are not bipartite) | `Lattice/Graph.lean` |
| `quantumIsingHamiltonian_eq_isingHamiltonianGeneric` | **generic-N bridge**: `quantumIsingHamiltonian N J h = isingHamiltonianGeneric (couplingOf (pathGraph (N+1)) (-J/2)) h`. The proof itself is the robust regression test | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |

| Lean name / location | Purpose |
|---|---|
| `LatticeSystem/Tests/Sanity.lean` | sanity-check `example` blocks for concrete small-N instances (Pauli arithmetic, spin-1/2 ladder actions, Heisenberg / Ising Hermiticity on small chains, graph-centric bridge identities) |
| decide-based property tests (in `Tests/Sanity.lean`) | universally-quantified properties verified by `decide` on small finite types (graph adjacency symmetry / irreflexivity / connectivity on `pathGraph n` and `cycleGraph n` for small `n`); real proofs, no `sorry` |

| `quantumIsingGibbsState_commute_hamiltonian` | `[╧Б_╬▓, H_Ising] = 0` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `quantumIsingGibbsExpectation_zero` | infinite-temperature closed form `тЯиAтЯй_0 = (1/dim) ┬╖ Tr A` (independent of `J, h`) | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `quantumIsingGibbsExpectation_im_of_isHermitian` | for Hermitian `O`, `(тЯиOтЯй_╬▓).im = 0` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `quantumIsingGibbsExpectation_commutator_hamiltonian` | conservation `тЯи[H_Ising, A]тЯй_╬▓ = 0` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `quantumIsingGibbsExpectation_hamiltonian_im` | `(тЯиH_IsingтЯй_╬▓).im = 0` (energy expectation is real) | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `quantumIsingGibbsExpectation_mul_hamiltonian_im` | for Hermitian `O`, `(тЯиH_Ising ┬╖ OтЯй_╬▓).im = 0` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `quantumIsingGibbsExpectation_hamiltonian_sq_im` | `(тЯиH_Ising^2тЯй_╬▓).im = 0` (energy-squared expectation real) | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `quantumIsingGibbsExpectation_hamiltonian_pow_im` | `(тЯиH_Ising^nтЯй_╬▓).im = 0` for any `n : тДХ` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `quantumIsingGibbsExpectation_anticommutator_im` | for Hermitian `A, B`, `(тЯиA┬╖B + B┬╖AтЯй_╬▓).im = 0` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `quantumIsingGibbsExpectation_commutator_re` | for Hermitian `A, B`, `(тЯиA┬╖B тИТ B┬╖AтЯй_╬▓).re = 0` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `quantumIsingGibbsHamiltonianVariance_im` | `(Var_╬▓(H_Ising)).im = 0` (energy variance real) | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `quantumIsing_partitionFn_im` | `(partitionFn ╬▓ H_Ising).im = 0` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `quantumIsingGibbsExpectation_ofReal_re_eq` | for Hermitian `O`, `((тЯиOтЯй_╬▓).re : тДВ) = тЯиOтЯй_╬▓` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `quantumIsingGibbsState_pow_trace` | `Tr(╧Б_╬▓^n) = Z(n╬▓) / Z(╬▓)^n` for the Ising Hamiltonian | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `quantumIsingGibbsExpectation_self_eq` | `тЯиH_IsingтЯй_╬▓ = -J ┬╖ тИС тЯи╧Г^z ╧Г^zтЯй_╬▓ + (-h) ┬╖ тИС тЯи╧Г^xтЯй_╬▓` (energy as bond + transverse-field decomposition) | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |

### Gibbs state (Tasaki ┬з3.3)

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, ┬з3.3.

All theorems in this module are fully proved with **zero `sorry`**.

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `gibbsExp ╬▓ H` | `exp(-╬▓H) := Matrix.exp (-╬▓ тАв H)` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_isHermitian` | `exp(-╬▓H)` is Hermitian (when `H` is Hermitian) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_zero` | `exp(-0┬╖H) = 1` (Tasaki ┬з3.3, pp. 75тАУ78) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_add` | `exp(-(╬▓тВБ+╬▓тВВ)H) = exp(-╬▓тВБH) ┬╖ exp(-╬▓тВВH)` (one-parameter group) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_add_of_commute_hamiltonians` | `exp(-╬▓(HтВБ+HтВВ)) = exp(-╬▓HтВБ) ┬╖ exp(-╬▓HтВВ)` for commuting `HтВБ, HтВВ` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_neg_mul_self` | `exp(╬▓H) ┬╖ exp(-╬▓H) = 1` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_self_mul_neg` | `exp(-╬▓H) ┬╖ exp(╬▓H) = 1` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_isUnit` | `exp(-╬▓H)` is invertible | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_ne_zero` | `exp(-╬▓H) тЙа 0` (corollary of `gibbsExp_isUnit`) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsState_ne_zero` | `╧Б_╬▓ тЙа 0` when `Z(╬▓) тЙа 0` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsState_inv` | `(╧Б_╬▓)тБ╗┬╣ = Z(╬▓) ┬╖ e^{╬▓H}` when `Z(╬▓) тЙа 0` (general matrix inverse, generalises `gibbsState_zero_inv`) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `partitionFn_smul_gibbsState_eq_gibbsExp` | `Z(╬▓) ┬╖ ╧Б_╬▓ = e^{-╬▓H}` when `Z(╬▓) тЙа 0` (canonical rescaled identity) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `partitionFn_mul_gibbsExpectation_eq` | `Z(╬▓) ┬╖ тЯиAтЯй_╬▓ = Tr(e^{-╬▓H} ┬╖ A)` when `Z(╬▓) тЙа 0` (canonical unnormalised expectation) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_natCast_mul` | `exp(-(n┬╖╬▓)H) = (exp(-╬▓H))^n` for `n : тДХ` (exact discrete semigroup identity) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_two_mul` | `exp(-(2╬▓)H) = exp(-╬▓H) ┬╖ exp(-╬▓H)` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_inv` | `(exp(-╬▓H))тБ╗┬╣ = exp(╬▓H)` (matrix inverse made explicit) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_intCast_mul` | `exp(-(n┬╖╬▓)H) = (exp(-╬▓H))^n` for `n : тДд` (integer-power extension) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `partitionFn ╬▓ H` | `Z := Matrix.trace (exp(-╬▓H))` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |

| `partitionFn_im_of_isHermitian` | for Hermitian `H`, `(partitionFn ╬▓ H).im = 0` (Z is real) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsState_mul_self_trace` | `Tr(╧Б_╬▓┬▓) = Z(2╬▓) / Z(╬▓)┬▓` (purity / R├йnyi-2 entropy precursor) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsState_pow_trace` | `Tr(╧Б_╬▓^n) = Z(n╬▓) / Z(╬▓)^n` for any `n : тДХ` (R├йnyi-n entropy precursor) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |

| `gibbsExpectation_zero` | `тЯиAтЯй_0 = (1/dim) ┬╖ Tr A` (high-temperature limit) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |

| `gibbsState_trace` | `Tr(╧Б) = 1` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsState_isHermitian` | `╧Б` is Hermitian | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |

| `gibbsExpectation_one` | `тЯи1тЯй = 1` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation_add` | `тЯиOтВБ + OтВВтЯй = тЯиOтВБтЯй + тЯиOтВВтЯй` (linearity in observable) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation_smul` | `тЯиc ┬╖ OтЯй = c ┬╖ тЯиOтЯй` (scalar linearity, `c : тДВ`) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation_neg` | `тЯи-OтЯй = -тЯиOтЯй` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation_sub` | `тЯиA - BтЯй = тЯиAтЯй - тЯиBтЯй` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation_sum` | `тЯитИС i тИИ s, f iтЯй = тИС i тИИ s, тЯиf iтЯй` (finite-sum linearity) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_commute_hamiltonian` | `[exp(-╬▓H), H] = 0` (Tasaki ┬з3.3, p. 80) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsState_commute_hamiltonian` | `[╧Б_╬▓, H] = 0`, i.e. `╧Б_╬▓` is stationary under the dynamics generated by `H` (Tasaki ┬з3.3, p. 80) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `Matrix.trace_mul_star_of_isHermitian` | `star (Tr(A ┬╖ B)) = Tr(A ┬╖ B)` for Hermitian `A, B : Matrix n n тДВ` (algebraic core, Gibbs-independent) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |

| `gibbsExpectation_mul_comm_of_commute_hamiltonian` | for any conserved `A` (`[A, H] = 0`), `тЯиA ┬╖ OтЯй_╬▓ = тЯиO ┬╖ AтЯй_╬▓` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |

| `gibbsVariance_eq_centered_sq` | `Var_╬▓(O) = тЯи(O тИТ тЯиOтЯй_╬▓ ┬╖ 1) ┬╖ (O тИТ тЯиOтЯй_╬▓ ┬╖ 1)тЯй_╬▓` (centered-square form, `Z тЙа 0`) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsCovariance ╬▓ H A B` | `Cov_╬▓(A, B) := тЯиA ┬╖ BтЯй_╬▓ тИТ тЯиAтЯй_╬▓ ┬╖ тЯиBтЯй_╬▓` (canonical-ensemble complex covariance) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |

| `gibbsCovariance_add_left` | `Cov_╬▓(AтВБ + AтВВ, B) = Cov_╬▓(AтВБ, B) + Cov_╬▓(AтВВ, B)` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsCovariance_add_right` | `Cov_╬▓(A, BтВБ + BтВВ) = Cov_╬▓(A, BтВБ) + Cov_╬▓(A, BтВВ)` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |

### Heisenberg chain (Tasaki ┬з3.5)

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, ┬з3.5, p. 89.

| Lean name | Statement | File |

| `LatticeSystem.Lattice.couplingOf G J` | the canonical pairwise coupling `╬Ы тЖТ ╬Ы тЖТ тДВ` of a `SimpleGraph G` with uniform edge weight `J`: returns `J` on edges of `G`, zero otherwise (graph-centric bridge) | `Lattice/Graph.lean` |
| `LatticeSystem.Lattice.couplingOf_symm` / `_self` / `_real` | symmetry (from `G.Adj` symmetry), vanishing on the diagonal (from irreflexivity), and reality (for real edge weight) | `Lattice/Graph.lean` |

| `openChainCoupling_sum_eq` | for any `N : тДХ`, `╬г_{x,y тИИ Fin (N+1)} openChainCoupling N J x y = -(2N ┬╖ J : тДВ)` (the bond-counting lemma: each of the `N` unordered nearest-neighbour bonds is counted in both orientations) | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |

### Perron-Frobenius theorem (`Math/PerronFrobenius.lean`, `Math/PerronFrobeniusPrimitive.lean`, `Math/CollatzWielandt.lean`, `Math/PerronFrobeniusMain.lean`)

Perron-Frobenius theorem for nonneg irreducible/primitive matrices (Issue #405, closed).
The sorry in `exists_pos_eigenvec_max` is eliminated via the Collatz-Wielandt port (PRs AтАУC).

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `Matrix.IsPrimitive.of_irreducible_pos_diagonal` | irreducible nonneg + positive diagonal тЖТ primitive (Seneta ┬з1.1, Prop. 1.3, p. 17) | `Math/PerronFrobeniusPrimitive.lean` |
| `CollatzWielandt.collatzWielandtFn` | CW function `min_{i\|x_i>0} (Ax)_i/x_i` (Seneta ┬з1.2, p. 27) | `Math/CollatzWielandt.lean` |
| `CollatzWielandt.le_any_ratio` | `CW(x) тЙд (Ax)_i/x_i` for `x_i > 0` | `Math/CollatzWielandt.lean` |
| `CollatzWielandt.le_mulVec` | fundamental inequality `CW(x)┬╖x тЙд Ax` | `Math/CollatzWielandt.lean` |
| `CollatzWielandt.smul_eq` | scale invariance `CW(cx) = CW(x)` for `c > 0` | `Math/CollatzWielandt.lean` |
| `CollatzWielandt.upperSemicontinuousOn` | CW is upper-semicontinuous on stdSimplex | `Math/CollatzWielandt.lean` |
| `CollatzWielandt.exists_maximizer` | CW attains its max on stdSimplex (EVT for USC, Seneta ┬з1.2, p. 28) | `Math/CollatzWielandt.lean` |
| `CollatzWielandt.eq_eigenvalue` | `CW(v) = r` when `Av = r┬╖v`, `v > 0` | `Math/CollatzWielandt.lean` |
| `CollatzWielandt.lt_of_all_ratios_gt` | all ratios `> c` тЯ╣ `CW(x) > c` | `Math/CollatzWielandt.lean` |
| `PerronFrobeniusMain.pos_of_nonneg_eigenvec` | irreducible nonneg + `Av = ╬╝v`, `v тЙе 0`, `v тЙа 0` тЯ╣ `v > 0` (standard propagation argument) | `Math/PerronFrobeniusMain.lean` |
| `PerronFrobeniusMain.exists_positive_eigenvector_of_primitive` | primitive nonneg тЯ╣ тИГ `r > 0`, `v > 0` with `Av = rv` (Seneta ┬з1.2, pp. 27тАУ28) | `Math/PerronFrobeniusMain.lean` |
| `PerronFrobeniusMain.exists_positive_eigenvector_of_irreducible` | irreducible nonneg тЯ╣ тИГ `r > 0`, `v > 0` with `Av = rv` (Seneta ┬з1.2, pp. 27тАУ28) | `Math/PerronFrobeniusMain.lean` |
| `exists_nonneg_eigenvec_max` | (**sorry**, retained for docs) symmetric nonneg max eigenvalue has nonneg eigenvector | `Math/PerronFrobenius.lean` |
| `exists_pos_eigenvec_max` | (**sorry-free**) irreducible nonneg Hermitian тЯ╣ max eigenvalue has strictly positive eigenvector | `Math/PerronFrobenius.lean` |
| `pos_eigenvec_unique` | strictly positive eigenvector unique up to positive scalar | `Math/PerronFrobenius.lean` |

References: E. Seneta, *Non-negative Matrices and Markov Chains* (3rd ed.), Springer 2006, ┬з1.2 (pp. 27тАУ28);
or4nge19/MCMC: `MCMC/PF/LinearAlgebra/Matrix/PerronFrobenius/`.

### Spin-`S` MarshallтАУLiebтАУMattis on the magnetization sector (Tasaki ┬з2.5 Theorem 2.2 generic S, sector form)

Generic-spin (`N = 2S`) version of Tasaki ┬з2.5 Theorem 2.2 applied to the
**magnetization-`M` sector** of the un-dressed antiferromagnetic
Heisenberg Hamiltonian on a bipartite graph. The sector subtype
`magConfigS V N M := { ╧Г : V тЖТ Fin (N + 1) // magSumS ╧Г = M }` is the
natural index type since the dressed Heisenberg matrix is irreducible
on each sector. The core sector-matrix API lives in
`Quantum/SpinS/DressedMatrixOnMagSector.lean`; the trailing
eigenvalue-uniqueness + complex-form MLM Theorem 2.2 statements
were moved to the companion
`Quantum/SpinS/DressedMatrixOnMagSectorEigenvalueUnique.lean` in
refactor #30 (PR #2829). Tracked in Issue #412.

| Lean name | Statement |
|---|---|
| `magConfigS V N M` | sector subtype of magnetization-`M` configurations (`Quantum/SpinS/MagConfig.lean`) |
| `RaiseLowerStepSMagSector G ╧Г ╧Д` / `RaiseLowerReachableSMagSector G` | bipartite raise/lower step lifted to `magConfigS` and its reflexive transitive closure (`Quantum/SpinS/MagConfig.lean`) |
| `raiseLowerReachableSMagSector_bipartiteCompleteGraph` | any two configurations in the same sector are reachable via raise/lower steps under the bipartite-intermediate hypothesis (Tasaki ┬з2.5 Property (iii) generic-S form) |
| `shiftedDressedSReMatrixOnMagSector A J N c M` | shifted dressed Heisenberg matrix `c┬╖1 - dressed_re` restricted to the sector via `Matrix.submatrix Subtype.val Subtype.val`, the input to PF irreducibility |
| `dressedHeisenbergSReMatrixOnMagSector A J N M` | dressed Heisenberg real-form matrix restricted to the sector |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianSReMatrixOnMagSector J N M` | un-dressed Heisenberg real-form matrix restricted to the sector |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianSMatrixOnMagSector J N M` | un-dressed Heisenberg COMPLEX matrix restricted to the sector |
| `isIrreducible_shiftedDressedSReMatrixOnMagSector` | `Matrix.IsIrreducible` for the shifted sector matrix (Tasaki ┬з2.5 ╬│-3 final, MLM PF input) |
| `exists_positive_eigenvector_shiftedDressedSReMatrixOnMagSector` | PF eigenvector existence for the shifted sector matrix (`r > 0`, `v > 0` componentwise) |
| `pos_eigenvec_unique_shiftedDressedSReMatrixOnMagSector` | PF eigenvector uniqueness on the shifted sector matrix (Tasaki ┬з2.5 nondegeneracy) |
| `exists_positive_eigenvector_dressedHeisenbergSReMatrixOnMagSector` | PF on the dressed sector matrix at eigenvalue `c - r` (Tasaki ┬з2.5 dressed-form ground state) |
| `pos_eigenvec_unique_dressedHeisenbergSReMatrixOnMagSector` | dressed sector eigenvector uniqueness at fixed eigenvalue (PR #856) |
| `pos_eigenvec_eigenvalue_unique_dressedHeisenbergSReMatrixOnMagSector` | dressed sector positive eigenvectors share the same eigenvalue (Rayleigh identity for symmetric matrices, PR #856) |
| `dressedHeisenbergSReMatrix_eq_marshallSign_mul_heisenberg` / `heisenbergHamiltonianSReMatrix_eq_marshallSign_mul_dressed` | matrix relations `dressed = sign┬╖sign┬╖heis` and inverse via `sign┬▓ = 1` (PR #853) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianSReMatrixOnMagSector_mulVec_of_dressed_eigenvec` | Marshall sign conjugation of dressed sector eigenvector to un-dressed Heisenberg sector eigenvector (PR #853) |
| `dressedHeisenbergSReMatrixOnMagSector_mulVec_of_heis_eigenvec` | inverse Marshall conjugation (PR #854) |
| `exists_marshallSign_eigenvector_heisenbergHamiltonianSReMatrixOnMagSector` | un-dressed Heisenberg sector ground-state existence with Marshall sign structure (PR #853) |
| `marshallPositive_eigenvec_unique_heisenbergHamiltonianSReMatrixOnMagSector` | un-dressed Heisenberg sector Marshall-positive eigenvector uniqueness at fixed eigenvalue (PR #854) |
| `marshallPositive_eigenvec_eigenvalue_unique_heisenbergHamiltonianSReMatrixOnMagSector` | un-dressed Heisenberg sector Marshall-positive eigenvalue uniqueness (PR #856) |
| `marshallLiebMattis_spinS_heisenbergSector_groundState` | bundled Tasaki ┬з2.5 Theorem 2.2 (existence + same-eigenvalue uniqueness, PR #855) |
| `marshallLiebMattis_spinS_heisenbergSector_groundState_full` | strongest bundled Tasaki ┬з2.5 Theorem 2.2: existence + forced eigenvalue uniqueness + eigenvector uniqueness (PR #859) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianSMatrixOnMagSector_isHermitian` | complex sector matrix is Hermitian for real coupling (PR #858) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianSMatrixOnMagSector_apply_eq_ofReal` | for real coupling, complex sector entries equal real-form entries embedded in `тДВ` (PR #857) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianSMatrixOnMagSector_mulVec_ofReal` | real тЖТ complex eigenvector lift (PR #858) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianSReMatrixOnMagSector_mulVec_re_of_complex_eigenvec` | complex тЖТ real real-part extraction (PR #861) |
| `exists_marshallSign_complexEigenvector_heisenbergHamiltonianSMatrixOnMagSector` | complex-form Tasaki ┬з2.5 Theorem 2.2 ground-state existence on the un-dressed quantum Heisenberg sector matrix (PR #860) |
| `marshallPositive_complexEigenvec_re_unique_heisenbergHamiltonianSMatrixOnMagSector` | complex-form Marshall-positive uniqueness via real-part extraction (PR #862) |
| `marshallLiebMattis_spinS_heisenbergSector_complexGroundState_full` | strongest bundled Tasaki ┬з2.5 Theorem 2.2 on the complex sector matrix (PR #863) |

The complex-form `marshallLiebMattis_spinS_heisenbergSector_complexGroundState_full`
is the COMPLEX-Hilbert-space form of Tasaki ┬з2.5 Theorem 2.2 in the
magnetization sector: the ground state of the un-dressed quantum
Heisenberg Hamiltonian restricted to the sector is unique (up to a
positive real scalar in its real part) and has the Marshall sign
structure `╬ж ╧Г := ((sign A ╧Г.1).re * v ╧Г : тДВ)` with `v > 0`.

References: H. Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, Springer 2020, ┬з2.5 Theorem 2.2 (pp. 39тАУ43); E. Seneta,
*Non-negative Matrices and Markov Chains* (3rd ed.), Springer 2006,
┬з1.2 (pp. 27тАУ28) for the underlying PerronтАУFrobenius theorem.

### Spin-`S` saturated ferromagnetic state (Tasaki ┬з2.4 generalised)

Generic-spin (`N = 2S`) version of Tasaki ┬з2.4 P1i for the
**saturated ferromagnet**: the all-aligned (constant-spin) basis
state `|╧Г_тКдтЯй = тКЧ_x |cтЯй` with `╧Г x = c` for all `x : V`. The two
extremal weights `c = 0` (highest weight, "all up") and
`c = Fin.last N` (lowest weight, "all down") are the highest- and
lowest-weight vectors of the `J_tot = |V|┬╖S = |V|┬╖N/2` irreducible
SU(2) representation in the multi-site Hilbert space. Tracked in
Issue #412; assembled in PRs #875тАУ#879. All theorems live in
`Quantum/SpinS/AllAlignedState.lean`.

| Lean name | Statement |
|---|---|
| `allAlignedConfigS V N c` | constant configuration `╧Г x = c` (PR #875) |
| `allAlignedStateS V N c` | basis state at constant `c`, equal to `basisVecS (allAlignedConfigS V N c)` (PR #875) |
| `magSumS_allAlignedConfigS` | `magSumS = |V|┬╖c.val` (PR #875) |
| `magEigenvalueS_allAlignedConfigS` | `magEigenvalueS = |V|┬╖N/2 тИТ |V|┬╖c` (PR #875) |

First framework step toward decomposing joint eigenspace elements into per-sector components for the final Tasaki ┬з2.4 Theorem 2.1 closure (PR #2765) |
| `magSubspaceS_apply_eq_zero_of_magEigenvalueS_ne` / `magProjFn_add` / `magProjFn_smul` / `matrix_entry_eq_zero_of_mulVec_basisVecS_mem_magSubspaceS` / `heisenbergHamiltonianS_mulVec_magProjFn_eq` | **magProjFn linearity + commutation with H**: support property of `magSubspaceS V N M` (vanishes off the magnetisation level), linearity of `magProjFn` in the vector argument, off-magnetisation matrix-entry vanishing for any magnetisation-preserving operator, and the Heisenberg commutation `H ┬╖ magProjFn M v = magProjFn M (H ┬╖ v)` via the matrix-entry vanishing applied to `H ┬╖ basisVecS ╧Д` (PR #1078) (PR #2766) |
| `totalSpinSSquared_mulVec_magProjFn_eq` / `magProjFn_mem_saturatedFerromagnetJointEigenspace` | **Casimir commutation + joint preservation for magProjFn**: `(┼Ь_tot)┬▓ ┬╖ magProjFn M v = magProjFn M ((┼Ь_tot)┬▓ ┬╖ v)` (same matrix-entry-vanishing argument as PR #2766, applied to `(┼Ь_tot)┬▓ ┬╖ basisVecS ╧Д` via PR #1078), and the joint preservation `magProjFn M v тИИ joint` for `v тИИ joint` combining the two commutations with `magProjFn_smul` (PR #2767) |
| `sum_magProjFn_eq` / `saturatedFerromagnetJointEigenspace_le_span_ladderIterateUp` / `saturatedFerromagnetJointEigenspace_eq_span_ladderIterateUp` | **ЁЯОп Tasaki ┬з2.4 Theorem 2.1 closure**: `joint = span (Set.range (ladderIterateUp V N))`. (1) Pointwise decomposition `v = ╬г_{k} magProjFn (m_max - k.val) v` (each `╧Г` has unique `magSumS ╧Г тИИ {0, ..., |V|N}` selecting one term). (2) `joint тКЖ span(ladderIterateUp)`: for `v тИИ joint`, each magnetisation component is in `joint тКУ H_{m_max - k.val} = span {ladderIterateUp V N k}` (PR #2764 + PR #2767). (3) Combined with reverse inclusion `span тКЖ joint` (PR #904) via `le_antisymm`. Identifies the saturated-ferromagnet joint eigenspace as exactly the `(2m_max + 1)`-dim irreducible SU(2) representation generated by the lowering operator from `|╧Г_тКдтЯй` (PR #2768) |
| `ladderIterateUp_span_finrank_eq_succ_card_mul_N` / `ladderIterateUp_span_le_saturatedFerromagnetJointEigenspace` | **the linear span of the ladder family has `Module.finrank тДВ = |V|┬╖N + 1 = 2m_max + 1`** (via `finrank_span_eq_card`); the span is contained in the joint (H, ┼Ь_tot┬▓)-eigenspace (PR #904, file `Quantum/SpinS/SaturatedLadderSpan.lean`) |
| `saturatedFerromagnetJointEigenspace_finrank_eq` | **operator-level dimension formula**: `Module.finrank тДВ (saturatedFerromagnetJointEigenspace J N) = |V|┬╖N + 1 = 2m_max + 1`. Direct corollary of the Theorem 2.1 closure (PR #2768): the joint eigenspace equals the linear span of the ladder iterates (PR #2768), whose finrank is `|V|┬╖N + 1` (PR #904). Promotes the lower bound `finrank тЙе |V|┬╖N + 1` (PR #903) to an equality at the operator level, identifying the saturated-ferromagnet joint eigenspace as the unique `(2m_max + 1)`-dimensional irreducible SU(2) representation (PR #2769) |
| `totalSpinSOpMinus_mulVec_ladderIterateUp_interior` / `totalSpinSOpMinus_mulVec_ladderIterateUp_last` / `saturatedFerromagnetJointEigenspace_totalSpinSOpMinus_invariant` | **`┼Ь^-_tot` action on ladder iterates + invariance**: for `k.val + 1 < |V|┬╖N + 1`, `┼Ь^-_tot ┬╖ ladderIterateUp V N k = ladderIterateUp V N тЯиk.val + 1, _тЯй` (shift); for `k = Fin.last _`, `┼Ь^-_tot ┬╖ ladderIterateUp V N (Fin.last _) = 0` (boundary annihilation via PR #905). Lifts to `Submodule.map (┼Ь^-_tot).mulVecLin (joint J N) тЙд joint J N` тАФ the operational SU(2)-irrep lowering side of the joint eigenspace identified in Theorem 2.1 (PR #2768) (PR #2770, file `Quantum/SpinS/SaturatedLadderLoweringInvariant.lean`) |
| `totalSpinSOpPlus_mulVec_ladderIterateUp_zero` / `totalSpinSOpPlus_mulVec_ladderIterateUp_succ` / `saturatedFerromagnetJointEigenspace_totalSpinSOpPlus_invariant` | **`┼Ь^+_tot` action on ladder iterates + invariance**: `┼Ь^+_tot ┬╖ ladderIterateUp V N тЯи0, _тЯй = 0` (top-weight annihilation via PR #877); for `j + 1 < |V|┬╖N + 1`, `┼Ь^+_tot ┬╖ ladderIterateUp V N тЯиj+1, _тЯй = ((j+1) ┬╖ (|V|┬╖N тИТ j)) тАв ladderIterateUp V N тЯиj, _тЯй` (Casimir-rearrangement scalar via PR #882 + PR #887 + PR #894 packaged in `totalSpinSOpPlus_mulVec_totalSpinSOpMinus_pow_succ_allAlignedStateS_zero`). Lifts to `Submodule.map (┼Ь^+_tot).mulVecLin (joint J N) тЙд joint J N` тАФ the operational SU(2)-irrep raising side of Theorem 2.1's joint eigenspace, completing the closure under both su(2) ladder generators (with PR #2770) (PR #2771, file `Quantum/SpinS/SaturatedLadderRaisingInvariant.lean`) |
| `totalSpinSOp1_eq_one_half_smul_plus_add_minus` / `totalSpinSOp2_eq_one_over_two_I_smul_plus_sub_minus` / `saturatedFerromagnetJointEigenspace_totalSpinSOp{1,2,3}_invariant` | **Full Cartesian SU(2) closure of the saturated joint eigenspace**: total-operator identities `┼Ь^(1)_tot = (1/2)тАв(┼Ь^+_tot + ┼Ь^-_tot)` and `┼Ь^(2)_tot = (1/(2I))тАв(┼Ь^+_tot тИТ ┼Ь^-_tot)` (lifted from the single-site definitions of `spinSOp1` / `spinSOp2` via `onSiteS_smul` + `onSiteS_add/sub`); `┼Ь^(1)_tot` and `┼Ь^(2)_tot` invariance reduce via these decompositions to the ladder invariances of PRs #2770 / #2771; `┼Ь^(3)_tot` invariance follows directly from `ladderIterateUp_mem_eigenspace` (each ladder iterate is an `┼Ь^z_tot`-eigenvector at eigenvalue `m_max тИТ k`, so its `┼Ь^z_tot`-image is a scalar multiple still in `span(ladderIterateUp) = joint J N`). Completes the full `su(2)`-module structure of the saturated joint eigenspace тАФ invariance under all generators тАФ confirming the operational identification with the `(2m_max + 1)`-dim irreducible representation, the operational closure of Tasaki ┬з2.4 Theorem 2.1 (PR #2772, file `Quantum/SpinS/SaturatedLadderCartesianInvariant.lean`) |
| `magSubspaceS_eq_bot_of_not_in_spectrum` / `magEigenvalueS_ne_neg_mMax_sub_one` / `totalSpinSOpMinus_pow_succ_card_mul_N_allAlignedStateS_zero` | for `M : тДВ` not in the spectrum of `┼Ь^z_tot`, `magSubspaceS V N M = тКе`; `тИТm_max тИТ 1` is outside the spectrum; **boundary annihilation** `(┼Ь^-_tot)^(|V|┬╖N + 1) ┬╖ |╧Г_тКдтЯй = 0` (PR #905, file `Quantum/SpinS/LadderBoundaryAnnihilation.lean`). Systems*, Springer 2020, ┬з2.4 (pp. 30тАУ37, spin-1/2 case).

### Single-mode fermion (P2 skeleton)

Phase 2 entry point: the canonical anticommutation algebra of a single
fermion mode acting on `тДВ┬▓` with computational basis
`|0тЯй` (vacuum) and `|1тЯй` (occupied).

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `fermionAnnihilation` | `c = !![0, 1; 0, 0] = |0тЯйтЯи1|` | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionCreation` | `cтАа = !![0, 0; 1, 0] = |1тЯйтЯи0|` | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionNumber` | `n = !![0, 0; 0, 1] = |1тЯйтЯи1|` | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionNumber_eq_creation_mul_annihilation` | `n = cтАа ┬╖ c` | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionAnnihilation_sq` | `c┬▓ = 0` | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionCreation_sq` | `(cтАа)┬▓ = 0` | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionAnticomm_self` | `c ┬╖ cтАа + cтАа ┬╖ c = 1` (single-mode CAR) | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionNumber_sq` | `n┬▓ = n` (idempotent number operator) | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionAnnihilation_conjTranspose` | `cс┤┤ = cтАа` | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
